Sliding window : when u are required to perform some activity on a fixed sub set of elements(WR2 size) belonging to some DS while adding and removing elements from it
        in a uniform manner ; consider such subsets as windows where the size of each window would always remain the same while the elements would vary in each step 
        That is to say new element would be sizeOfSubSet+1 and removed element would be k -1 Order will never be altered .Longest , Largest /SMallest Element/subsequence/subset

ARRAY vs LINKED LIST 

We know that the elements of an [] have contiguous memory location which means if some new element is inserted at the head of the [] , it will mean shifting the rest of the elements 
to the address of their NEIGHBOURING elements which in worse case would be have an O(n) complexity . BUT Linked List possesses elements as part of individual nodes containing 
a reference to the next node apart from the element value itself . ' . complexity reduces to O(1) Another good thing , we don't need to hold the entire LInked list as seen in case of [] 
Just the head of the Linked List is fine  
Whereas in case of a Doubly linked List where nodes also contain the memory address of the previous node as well , insertion at the end of the link would be easier than a singly 
Linked List 

Time and Space Complexity Tips : 
When we add T.C. like this []-> O(n) + ""->O(n) + Stack->O(n) in the end its linear itself that is O(n)+O(n)+O(n) = O(n) 
When we add  S.C. --->                                                                                 -->                                 will also be linear

    	public ListNode moveMiddleToHead(ListNode head) {
             if (head == null || head.next == null) {
            return head; 
        }
        
        ListNode slow = head;
        ListNode fast = head;
        ListNode prevSlow = null;
        
        while (fast != null && fast.next != null) {
            prevSlow = slow;
            slow = slow.next;
            fast = fast.next.next;
        }
        prevSlow.next = slow.next; 
        slow.next = head; 
        head = slow;         
        return head;
	}

Detect cycle in linkedList 
BUG where will u if() for the cyclic condition ? --->                                                                                                                               u were doubtful if it has to be inside the while loop or outside of it                                                                                              even if you know inside of it then what shall be order ?     Floyd's algo 
    public boolean linkedListCycle(ListNode head) {
        if(head == null || head.next == null) return false;
        ListNode slow = head;
        ListNode fast = head;
        while(fast != null && fast.next != null){
            if(slow == fast) return true;
            slow = slow.next;
            fast = fast.next.next;
        }
        return false;
    }
T.C. O(n)

Approach 
             Create a dummy node to serve as the head of the merged list
        Pointer to traverse the merged list        
         Traverse both lists and compare nodes to merge them
         Append the remaining nodes of the non-empty list
         Return the head of the merged list
            ListNode dummy = new ListNode(0);
        ListNode current = dummy; 
        while (l1 != null && l2 != null) {
            if (l1.val < l2.val) {
                current.next = l1;
                l1 = l1.next;
            } else {
                current.next = l2;
                l2 = l2.next;
            } 
            current = current.next;
        }
        
        if (l1 != null) {
            current.next = l1;
        }
        if (l2 != null) {
            current.next = l2;
        }
        
        return dummy.next;
    }        

Find Duplicates in a LinkedList 
    	    BUGS
		how to add elements inside of a set 
		intial and end positioning of inner and outer pointers n the way they traverse
		explain in terms of code how they change positions at specific situations 
		condition for unvisited nodes 
	   hashSet to track visited nodes. Why hash because Set can have O(n) for retreiveing elements but hash has O(1) similar to hashMap 
		public static void removeDuplicates(ListNode head)
	{
             if (head == null) {
            return ;
        }
        
        HashSet<Integer> seen = new HashSet<>();
        ListNode prev = null;
        ListNode curr = head;
        
        while (curr != null) {
            if (!seen.contains(curr.val)) {
                seen.add(curr.val);
                prev = curr;
            } else {
                prev.next = curr.next;
            }
            curr = curr.next;
        }
    }

        public ListNode reverseLinkedList(ListNode head){
    
    ListNode curr = head; 
    ListNode prev = null;
    while(curr != null){
        ListNode temp = curr.next;
        curr.next = prev;
        prev = curr;
        curr = temp;
    } 
    return prev;
    }

            ListNode temp = ☝️.next;
            ☝️.next = 👈;
            👈 = ☝️;

        }

    }
 Recursive solution: 
    Approach: 
        we need to ensure that adjacent node points to the current node and delete the reference existing in current referring to the right node since 
        things are to the left now meaning this current node shall also be pointing to its left in the recursive call  
    BUG: 
        discuss recursive call positioning in terms of backtracking                                                                                                                                     it would be better to start reversing from the end node because moving to tail will help us manipulating it to head i.e. when we come across a null current.next node we need to update head to current node so pass both of em as parameters not touching the head in any situation

    public static void reverseLinkedList(ListNode head,ListNode current){
        if(current == null) return;
        ListNode next=current.next;
        if(next==null){
            head=current;
            return;
        }
        reverseLinkedList(head,next);// you had passed current.next here which is not wrong but would have been redundant for sure
        next.next=current;//passed as reference therefore no issues of checking 
        current.next=null;
    }
PALINDROME LOGIC (LL) :
        o Naive Brute Force : 
            o Fetch all node.val s from Linked it in a temp[] while traversing it linearly 
            o Store its reverse in another rev[] and later check if its ele's are the same or not 
            o T.C. : Linear O(n);
            CONS:
                o S.C. : O(n) of temp[] + rev[] after avoiding THE CONSTANTS IN WORST CASE
                o Solution is below which does not use any extra auxillary space.
    Mid pint technique  
        DOUBT 
        What if the linked list is too long then finding the mid-point using floyd's algo will work ? 
        Size of LL being odd,even determining speed of fast pointer AND calculation of mid as seen in case of 
        regular string palindromic questions where odd length had a diff execution than even length 
         o traverse the data halfway through then we can reduce the time ! 
         o get the mid-point by fast and slow pointers meaning if 
            our fast pointer is 2x slow than by the time fast ends its traversal our slow would have reached the mid  
         o at this point slow points 2 the mid while fast is at the end 
         o Second half can be reversed using the reverse LL as talked about previously  
         Then use lead-lag pointer 
         o Lead-Lag pointer shall traverse at the same speed and at every step ele at indices lead=fast and lag=slow shall have the same ele if its a palindrome 
         o we will continue until the lead reaches null or end of LL then if ele's matched than its a palindrome

o Loop pattern
o Sorting pattern

Delete middle node from Linked List 
/*
The ListNode class is implemented as follows:
public class ListNode {
   public int val; 
   public ListNode next;
   public ListNode(int x) { val = x; next = null; }
}
*/

class Solution {
    public static void deleteGivenNode(ListNode node) {
      node.val = node.next.val;
        
        // Delete the next node by skipping it
        node.next = node.next.next;
    }
    
    // Helper method to create linked list from array
    public static ListNode createList(int[] arr) {
        if (arr.length == 0) return null;
        
        ListNode head = new ListNode(arr[0]);
        ListNode current = head;
        
        for (int i = 1; i < arr.length; i++) {
            current.next = new ListNode(arr[i]);
            current = current.next;
        }
        
        return head;
    }
    
    // Helper method to find node at position K
    public static ListNode findNodeAtPosition(ListNode head, int k) {
        ListNode current = head;
        for (int i = 1; i < k && current != null; i++) {
            current = current.next;
        }
        return current;
    }
    
    // Helper method to print linked list
    public static void printList(ListNode head) {
        ListNode current = head;
        while (current != null) {
            System.out.print(current.val);
            if (current.next != null) {
                System.out.print(" ");
            }
            current = current.next;
        }
        System.out.println();
    }
21,Merge Two Sorted Lists
        Merge two sorted linked lists into one sorted linked list, returning the head.
        class Solution {
        public ListNode mergeTwoLists(ListNode list1, ListNode list2) {
            ListNode dummy = new ListNode(-1);
            ListNode tail = dummy;

            while (list1 != null && list2 != null) {
                if (list1.val <= list2.val) {
                    tail.next = list1;
                    list1 = list1.next;
                } else {
                    tail.next = list2;
                    list2 = list2.next;
                }
                tail = tail.next;
            }

            tail.next = (list1 != null) ? list1 : list2;
            return dummy.next;
        }
    }

141,Linked List Cycle
    Given the head of a linked list, determine if the list contains a cycle.
    class Solution {
    public boolean hasCycle(ListNode head) {
        if (head == null) return false;
        ListNode slow = head, fast = head;
        while (fast != null && fast.next != null) {
            slow = slow.next;
            fast = fast.next.next;
            if (slow == fast) return true;
        }
        return false;
    }
}

142,Linked List Cycle II
    Return the node where the cycle begins (if one exists).
    After detecting a meeting point using Floyd’s algorithm,
move one pointer to head and advance both by one — they’ll meet at the cycle start.
BUG: You should be traversing the slow and fast pointers alone not the head which you did out of mistake
class Solution {
    public ListNode detectCycle(ListNode head) {
        if (head == null) return null;
        ListNode slow = head, fast = head;
        while (fast != null && fast.next != null) {
            slow = slow.next;
            fast = fast.next.next;
            if (slow == fast) {
                slow = head;
                while (slow != fast) {
                    slow = slow.next;
                    fast = fast.next;
                }
                return slow;
            }
        }
        return null;
    }
}

I. First Intuition: 
    Mono(1)tonic(tone/direction): Note that. Four questions which require a specific kind of ordering, either increasing or decreasing, should be referred to as monotonic series and therefore we can use stack in our solutions
    Monotonic stack is a data structure which. 18 cent stores elements in a specific order, either slightly increasing or strictly decreasing. 
    .'. Next greater/smaller, previous greater/smaller, largest rectangle, stock span probem, temperature days to wait histogram problems
II. Second Intuition: 
    Simulation: are the eles interacting with one another ? That interaction leads to what ? Elimination of one ?

496 Next Greater Element I  (LC had 2 arrays )  
Brute Force Approach
    n x m
o Brute Force 2 loops(1for 2nd reverse Iterating while ) leading to O(n2) : int ans[] = new int[nums1.length]; for i -> nums.length { 
    int greaterEle=-1; j= nums2.length -1;while(  j>=0 && nums2[j] != nums1[i]){//C that == condition beautifully being handled   
    if(nums2[j] > nums1[i]){ greaterEele = nums2[j];} j --;//I should be adding this up to the resulting array isn't it ??  
} }  
Optimized Approach: 
    n*m
    instead of traversing the nums1 array to look for their element's respective index in the second array we use a 
    monotonic decreasing stack to track which elements in nums2 actually having a next greater element to their right and store them as values in a hash map
    while the element itself serves as the key. Traversing nums2 When we come across an element which is greater than the topmost element(smallest) of stack we 
    pop it out top element's next greater element is the current element of nums2. otherwise we keep pushing elements to the stack 
    Then while 
o LC - On to the right of the curr element not the same index   
BUG: you keep indexes to the stack n name instead of nums2 ele
Sol: 
        public int[] nextGreaterElement(int[] nums1, int[] nums2) {
        Stack<Integer> dec = new Stack<>();
        Map<Integer,Integer> nge = new HashMap<>();
        int[] ans = new int[nums1.length];
        for(int i = 0 ; i < nums2.length ; i ++){
            while(!dec.isEmpty() && dec.peek() < nums2[i]){
                int smaller = dec.pop();
                nge.put(smaller,nums2[i]);
            }
            dec.push(nums2[i]);
        }
        while(!dec.isEmpty()){
            int smaller = dec.pop();
            nge.put(smaller,-1);
        }
        for(int i = 0 ; i < nums1.length ; i ++){
            ans[i]=nge.get(nums1[i]);
        }
        return ans;
    }

LeetCode #,Problem Name
283,Move Zeroes
    Given an integer array nums, move all 0s to the end while maintaining the relative order of non-zero elements.
    You must do this in-place, without making a copy.
    Intuition: 
        Pretty simple, keep a var insertPos = 0; then traverse the array for non-zero and keep arr[insertPos++] = non-zero Element. 
        while insertPos continues to be smaller than num's length keep adding zero to num and increase insertPos by 1 you can do this in one line -->                                                                   nums[insertPos ++] = 0;
        class Solution {
        public void moveZeroes(int[] nums) {
            int insertPos = 0;

            for (int num : nums) {
                if (num != 0) {
                    nums[insertPos++] = num;
                }
            }

            while (insertPos < nums.length) {
                nums[insertPos++] = 0;
            }
        }
    }

27,Remove Element
    Given an integer array nums and an integer val, remove all instances of val in-place.
    Return the new length of the array after removal.
    (The order of elements can change, but not required here.)
            class Solution {
            public int removeElement(int[] nums, int val) {
                int k = 0; // index to place the next valid element
                for (int i = 0; i < nums.length; i++) {
                    if (nums[i] != val) {
                        nums[k++] = nums[i];
                    }
                }
                return k;
            }
        }

344,Reverse String
        class Solution {
        public void reverseString(char[] s) {
            int left = 0, right = s.length - 1;
            while (left < right) {
                char temp = s[left];
                s[left] = s[right];
                s[right] = temp;
                left++;
                right--;
            }
        }

    BUG: First few lines of the func ???                                                                                                                                                                                                                        you will forget about k for sure along with early returns --->                                                                                  k = k % n;

        public void rotate(int[] nums, int k) {
        int n = nums.length;
        if(n == 0) return;
        k = k % n;
        if(k==0) return ;
        reverse(nums,0,n-1);
        reverse(nums,0,k-1);
        reverse(nums,k,n-1);
     }   
     public void reverse(int[] nums,int start,int end){
        while(start<end){
            int temp = nums[start];
            nums[start] = nums[end];
            nums[end] = temp;
            start ++;
            end --;
        }
    }

977,Squares of a Sorted Array
    Given a sorted array nums (may contain negatives), return a new array of the squares of each number, also sorted in non-decreasing order.
        class Solution {
        public int[] sortedSquares(int[] nums) {
            int n = nums.length;
            int[] result = new int[n];
            int left = 0, right = n - 1, pos = n - 1;

            while (left <= right) {
                int leftSq = nums[left] * nums[left];
                int rightSq = nums[right] * nums[right];
                if (leftSq > rightSq) {
                    result[pos--] = leftSq;
                    left++;
                } else {
                    result[pos--] = rightSq;
                    right--;
                }
            }

            return result;
        }
    }

167,Two Sum II – Input Array Is Sorted
    Given a 1-indexed sorted array of integers numbers, find two numbers such that they add up to a target number.
    Return the indices as an array [i, j] (1-based).
        class Solution {
        public int[] twoSum(int[] numbers, int target) {
            int left = 0, right = numbers.length - 1;

            while (left < right) {
                int sum = numbers[left] + numbers[right];
                if (sum == target) {
                    return new int[]{left + 1, right + 1};
                } else if (sum < target) {
                    left++;
                } else {
                    right--;
                }
            }

            return new int[]{-1, -1}; // should not reach here per problem constraints
        }
    }

392,Is Subsequence https://leetcode.com/problems/is-subsequence/

        isSubsequence("aaaaa", "ahbc")  // false (multiple a's available so in total 5 a should be present)
        isSubsequence("", "abc")       // true (empty string is subsequence)
        isSubsequence("abc", "")       // false  
        isSubsequence("ace", "abcde")  // true (skip b and d)
        isSubsequence("aec", "abcde")  // false (c comes before e in s)
    Solution:
        Mention the pointer moving condition for em both -->                                                                                                                                                    you thought IF they match the right pointer will move ELSE left moves --> first guess was to replace the pointer ++ statements which got you right answer but failed for the test case "aaaaaa" "ahbc" meaning --->                                                             we move to the right for the second string at all situations
        public boolean isSubsequence(String s, String t) {
        int left = 0;
        int right = 0 ; 
        while(left < s.length() && right < t.length()){
            if(s.charAt(left) == t.charAt(right)){
                left ++;
            }
                right ++;
        }
        return left == s.length();
        }

11,Container With Most Water- https://leetcode.com/problems/container-with-most-water/description/
   Optimized
        NOTE: Improved version would be to avoid re-checking already checked values which shall bring down the complexity to log n which isn't good for small arrays but works way better than below solution for huge arrays
        public int maxArea(int[] height) {
        int currArea = 0;
        int maxArea = 0;
        int left = 0 ;
        int right = height.length - 1;
        while(left < right){
            currArea = (right - left) * Math.min(height[left],height[right]);
            maxArea = Math.max(currArea, maxArea);
            if(height[left] < height[right]) left ++;
            else right --;
        }
        return maxArea;
         }

15,3Sum
    Given an integer array nums, find all unique triplets [a, b, c] such that
    a + b + c == 0.
    No duplicate triplets allowed.
    import java.util.*;
    class Solution {
        public List<List<Integer>> threeSum(int[] nums) {
            List<List<Integer>> res = new ArrayList<>();
            Arrays.sort(nums);

            for (int i = 0; i < nums.length - 2; i++) {
                if (i > 0 && nums[i] == nums[i - 1]) continue; // skip duplicate a's

                int left = i + 1, right = nums.length - 1;
                while (left < right) {
                    int sum = nums[i] + nums[left] + nums[right];
                    if (sum == 0) {
                        res.add(Arrays.asList(nums[i], nums[left], nums[right]));
                        left++;
                        right--;
                        while (left < right && nums[left] == nums[left - 1]) left++; // skip duplicates
                        while (left < right && nums[right] == nums[right + 1]) right--;
                    } else if (sum < 0) {
                        left++;
                    } else {
                        right--;
                    }
                }
            }

            return res;
        }
    }

53 Maxium subarray sum - https://leetcode.com/problems/maximum-subarray/

        public int maxSubArray(int[] nums) {
        int maxSum = nums[0];
        int currentSum = nums[0];
        for(int curr=1; curr<nums.length ; curr ++){
           currentSum = Math.max(nums[curr],nums[curr] + currentSum);
           maxSum = Math.max(currentSum,maxSum);
        }
        return maxSum;
        }   

209,Minimum Size Subarray Sum
    Given an array of positive integers nums and integer target,
    find the smallest length of a contiguous subarray whose sum ≥ target.
    If none exists, return 0.
        class Solution {
        public int minSubArrayLen(int target, int[] nums) {
            int left = 0, sum = 0, minLen = Integer.MAX_VALUE;

            for (int right = 0; right < nums.length; right++) {
                sum += nums[right];

                while (sum >= target) {
                    minLen = Math.min(minLen, right - left + 1);
                    sum -= nums[left++];
                }
            }

            return (minLen == Integer.MAX_VALUE) ? 0 : minLen;
        }
    }

3,Longest Substring Without Repeating Chars
    Given a string s, find the length of the longest substring without repeating characters.
    import java.util.*;

    class Solution {
        public int lengthOfLongestSubstring(String s) {
            Map<Character, Integer> map = new HashMap<>();
            int left = 0, maxLen = 0;

            for (int right = 0; right < s.length(); right++) {
                char c = s.charAt(right);

                if (map.containsKey(c)) {
                    left = Math.max(left, map.get(c) + 1); // move left past duplicate
                }

                map.put(c, right);
                maxLen = Math.max(maxLen, right - left + 1);
            }

            return maxLen;
        }
    }

Fruit Into Baskets
    You have an array fruits where each fruit type is represented by an integer.
    You can carry at most 2 types of fruit.
    Find the length of the longest subarray that contains at most 2 distinct numbers.
    import java.util.*;
    class Solution {
        public int totalFruit(int[] fruits) {
            Map<Integer, Integer> map = new HashMap<>();
            int left = 0, max = 0;

            for (int right = 0; right < fruits.length; right++) {
                map.put(fruits[right], map.getOrDefault(fruits[right], 0) + 1);

                while (map.size() > 2) {
                    map.put(fruits[left], map.get(fruits[left]) - 1);
                    if (map.get(fruits[left]) == 0) map.remove(fruits[left]);
                    left++;
                }

                max = Math.max(max, right - left + 1);
            }

            return max;
        }
    }

        public boolean containsDuplicate(int[] nums) {
        //pass to a set
        // if set size 

        //frequencies with hash map
        Set<Integer> set = new HashSet<>();
        for(int i = 0 ; i < nums.length ; i ++){
            set.add(nums[i]);
        }
        if(set.size() != nums.length){
            return true;
        }
        return false;
    }
    BUT BETTER ONE would have been 
        class Solution {
        public boolean containsDuplicate(int[] nums) {
            HashSet<Integer> seen = new HashSet<>();

            for (int num : nums) {
                // If num is already in set, we found a duplicate
                if (seen.contains(num)) {
                    return true;
                }
                // Add num to set for future checks
                seen.add(num);
            }
            return false;  // No duplicates found
        }
        }
    AN EVEN BETTER ONE WOULD HAVE BEEN UN-KNOWN 
        class Solution {
            public boolean containsDuplicate(int[] nums) {
                HashSet<Integer> seen = new HashSet<>();

                for (int num : nums) {
                    // add() returns false if element already exists
                    if (!seen.add(num)) {
                        return true;
                    }
                }
                return false;
            }
        }

                  public void setZeroes(int[][] matrix) {
                        int rows = matrix.length;
                        int cols = matrix[0].length;

                        List<int[]> zeros = new ArrayList<>();

                        for(int i = 0; i < rows; i++){
                            for(int j = 0; j < cols; j++){
                                if(matrix[i][j] == 0){
                                    zeros.add(new int[]{i, j});
                                }
                            }
                        }

                        // 2. Mark rows & columns of collected zeros
                        for(int[] pos : zeros){
                            int row = pos[0], col = pos[1];

                            // set row
                            for(int c = 0; c < cols; c++){
                                if(matrix[row][c] != 0){
                                    matrix[row][c] = 0;
                                }
                            }

                            // set column
                            for(int r = 0; r < rows; r++){
                                if(matrix[r][col] != 0){
                                    matrix[r][col] = 0;
                                }
                            }
                        }
                    }
    Optimal 
        class Solution {
            public void setZeroes(int[][] matrix) {
                int rows = matrix.length;
                int cols = matrix[0].length;

                boolean firstRowZero = false;
                boolean firstColZero = false;

                // 1. Check first row for zero
                for (int j = 0; j < cols; j++) {
                    if (matrix[0][j] == 0) {
                        firstRowZero = true;
                        break;
                    }
                }

                // 2. Check first column for zero
                for (int i = 0; i < rows; i++) {
                    if (matrix[i][0] == 0) {
                        firstColZero = true;
                        break;
                    }
                }

                // 3. Use first row/column as markers
                for (int i = 1; i < rows; i++) {
                    for (int j = 1; j < cols; j++) {
                        if (matrix[i][j] == 0) {
                            matrix[i][0] = 0;   // mark row
                            matrix[0][j] = 0;   // mark column
                        }
                    }
                }

                // 4. Apply marks to set zeroes
                for (int i = 1; i < rows; i++) {
                    for (int j = 1; j < cols; j++) {
                        if (matrix[i][0] == 0 || matrix[0][j] == 0) {
                            matrix[i][j] = 0;
                        }
                    }
                }

                // 5. Handle first row
                if (firstRowZero) {
                    for (int j = 0; j < cols; j++) {
                        matrix[0][j] = 0;
                    }
                }

                // 6. Handle first column
                if (firstColZero) {
                    for (int i = 0; i < rows; i++) {
                        matrix[i][0] = 0;
                    }
                }
            }
        }

Diameter of a binary tree - https://leetcode.com/problems/diameter-of-binary-tree/
PENDING DSA use without an additional private int diameter variable 
Recursive
Intuition : 
Bugs : 
Previously diameter was returning no. of nodes but we want edges instead so -->                                                                                                                                                                                                         decrease diameter value by 1 
Solution :  
    public int diameterOfBinaryTree(TreeNode root) {
      return calculateDiameter(root).diameter;
    }
    private Pair calculateDiameter(TreeNode root) {
        if (root == null) {
            return new Pair(0, 0);
        }
        Pair left = calculateDiameter(root.left);
        Pair right = calculateDiameter(root.right);
        int depth = Math.max(left.depth, right.depth) + 1;
        int diameter = Math.max(Math.max(left.diameter, right.diameter), left.depth + right.depth);
        return new Pair(depth, diameter);
    }
    private static class Pair {
        int depth;
        int diameter;
        Pair(int depth, int diameter) {
            this.depth = depth;
            this.diameter = diameter;
        }
    }

        public int maxDepth(TreeNode root) {
        if(root == null) return 0 ;
        int leftDepth = maxDepth(root.left);
        int rightDepth = maxDepth(root.right);
        return 1 + Math.max(leftDepth,rightDepth);
        }

Solution :
            public int maxDepth(TreeNode root) {
        if(root == null) return 0 ;
        Stack<TreeNode> dfs = new Stack<>();
        Stack<Integer> depth = new Stack<>();
        dfs.push(root);
        depth.push(1);
        int maxDepth = 0;
        while(!dfs.isEmpty()){
            TreeNode currNode = dfs.pop();
            int currDepth = depth.pop();
            maxDepth = Math.max(maxDepth,currDepth);
            if(currNode.right != null){
                dfs.push(currNode.right);
                depth.push(currDepth + 1);
            }
            if(currNode.left != null){
                dfs.push(currNode.left);
                depth.push(currDepth + 1);
            }
        }
        return maxDepth;
        }

Solution : 
    public List<Integer> preorderTraversal(TreeNode root) {
        if(root == null) return new ArrayList<>();
        List<Integer> ans = new ArrayList<>();
        preOrder(root,ans);
        return ans;   
    }
    private void preOrder(TreeNode node,List<Integer> ans){
        if(node == null) return ;
        ans.add(node.val);
        preOrder(node.left,ans);
        preOrder(node.right,ans);
    }

                ans.add(curr.val);
                while( curr != null){//curr.left or simply curr  ? 
                    dfs.push(curr.left);//felt like it should be curr here 
                    curr = curr.left;//so here left as seen in non-morris inOrder iterative traversal ?? 
                }
                dfs.push(curr.right);//felt like it should be curr here 
                curr = curr.right;
            }
            return ans;
   } 

T.C. : 
    O(n) each node is visited once 
S.C. : 
    O(h) h = it might end up containing all the nodes of the Tree  
    height of the BST which is the longest distance between the root and last leaf node (since first Left then right )
    worst case with a highly unbalanced tree (left skewed tree ) the space complexity becomes O(h)

Solution  :  
        public List<Integer> preorderTraversal(TreeNode root) { 
        if(root == null) return new ArrayList<>(); 
        List<Integer> ans = new ArrayList<>(); 
        Stack<TreeNode> dfs=new Stack<>(); 
        dfs.push(root); 
        while(!dfs.isEmpty()){ 
            TreeNode curr = dfs.pop(); 
            ans.add(curr.val);
            if(curr.right != null) dfs.push(curr.right);
            if(curr.left != null) dfs.push(curr.left);
        }
        return ans;
    }

Solution : 
    public List<Integer> postorderTraversal(TreeNode root) {
        List<Integer> ans = new ArrayList<>();
        return postOrder(root,ans);
    }
        private List<Integer> postOrder(TreeNode root,List<Integer> ans){
        if(root == null) return ans;
        postOrder(root.right,ans);
        postOrder(root.left,ans);
        ans.add(root.val);
        return ans;
        }

Solution : 
    public List<Integer> postorderTraversal(TreeNode root) { 
        if(root == null) return new ArrayList<>(); 
        List<Integer> ans = new ArrayList<>(); 
        Stack<TreeNode> stk=new Stack<>(); 
        stk.push(root); 
        while(!stk.isEmpty()){ 
            TreeNode peek = stk.peek(); 
            if(peek.left == null && peek.right == null){ 
                TreeNode pop = stk.pop(); 
                ans.add(pop.val); 
            }else{ 
                if(peek.right != null){ 
                stk.push(peek.right);
                peek.right = null;
                }
                if(peek.left != null){ 
                stk.push(peek.left);
                peek.left = null;
                }    
            }
        }
        return ans;
    }

    public List<Integer> inorderTraversal(TreeNode root) {
        if(root == null) return new ArrayList<>();
        List<Integer> ans =new ArrayList<>();
        inOrder(root,ans);
        return ans;
    }
    private void inOrder(TreeNode node,List<Integer> ans){
        if(node == null) return ;
        inOrder(node.left,ans);
        ans.add(node.val);
        inOrder(node.right,ans);
    }

Solution : 
        public List<Integer> inorderTraversal(TreeNode root){
        List<Integer> ans = new ArrayList<>();
       Stack<TreeNode> dfs = new Stack<>();
       TreeNode curr = root;
       while(!dfs.isEmpty() || curr != null){ 
        while(curr != null){ 
            dfs.push(curr); 
            curr = curr.left; 
        } 
        curr = dfs.pop(); 
        ans.add(curr.val); 
        curr = curr.right;
       }
       return ans;
    }

Intuition : 
o We know that recursively calling the SAME () to refer 2 the curr.left child lead 2 
o returning back to the root 
o we want a way to return back 2 the root SINCE NO RECURSION HERE 
(OTHERWISE will have to use Stack which shall increase the S.C.) 
o This way will be the rightMost non-null child(predecessor) OF THE left child of the current node (i.e. curr.left) 
o i.e. think then --->                                                                                                                                                                      when predecessor != null => predecessor.right = curr where this predecessor shall belong to SOME LEFT CHILD of curr ALMOST LIKE when curr.left != null go right when left.right != null then predecessor.right = curr 
o Now that we have a way to return back to the rootOR current(which is predecessor.right) ;we can remove the reference between curr and its left child i.e. curr.left 
o We will move the curr pointer by curr = curr.left; and look for its left child letZ say curr.left 
o EVEN WHEN no right child exists for this recently visited curr.left node we will connect this curr.left(now this is predecessor) it to this curr itself !     
o Again remove the reference b/t curr and curr.left since we can return back to root(which is curr) from the predecessor(which was the left child this time )
o When no left child found we print the node AND GO TO THE RIGHT which is where the predecessor shall lead us OTHERWISE will be having a right child anyway in the List<Integer> whatever might b the return type  
NOW Left->Root-> Right child shall be the middle node or In node of inOrder therefore we print it 2 and check for its left child as usual 
o There can be a possibility that no left child exists for this middle node where we were directed from the predecessor 
o Now we can move to the right since no left child and if right child is also null we will stop our inOrder traversal 
T.C. : we will have to visit every node ONCE . ' . O(n);
S.C : no recursion , no stack so no maximum depth of stack scenario arises . ' . O(1);

Morris :  
    public List<Integer> inorderTraversal(TreeNode root){     
        List<Integer> ans = new ArrayList<>();
        TreeNode curr = root;
        while(curr != null){
            if(curr.left == null){
                ans.add(curr.val);
                curr = curr.right;
            }else{
                TreeNode predecessor = curr.left;
                while(predecessor.right != null){
                    predecessor = predecessor.right;
                }
                if(predecessor != null){
                    TreeNode temp = curr;
                    predecessor.right = curr;
                    curr = curr.left;
                    temp.left = null;
                }else{
                    curr = curr.left;
                }
                
            }
        }        
        return ans;
     }

o BINARY SEARCH - search in sorted/alphabetically?? [] with log n complexity  
search in sorted array 
Complete the function search in the code editor for a language of your choice.

search has the following parameters :

nums : An array of numbers having its values in a rotated sorted order

target : An integer representing the number to be searched in nums

search returns :

int : An integer denoting the index of the target to be searched. If target not present returns -1.


Assume the array doesn’t have duplicates.

Input format
There are Q+3 lines of input.

First line will have a single integer N denoting the size of the array.

Second line will contain N space separated integers.

Third line will contain a single integer Q denoting the number of targets to be searched..

Next Q lines will have a single integer,X in each line denoting the target value. You have to search for each of these target values in turn.

Output format
One line per output for each target search, with -1 or the index at which the integer is found.

Constraints
1 <= N <= 10^6 where N denotes the size of the input array

1 <= A[i] <= 10^9 where A[i] denotes the ith element of the input array

1 <= Q <= 10^6 where Q denotes the number of targets to be searched

1 <= X <= 10^9 where X denotes the target element to be search

Sample Input 1
7

4 5 6 9 10 2 3

2

3

8

Sample Output 1
6

-1

Explanation 1
The element 3 is found in the array at index 6. Element 8 is not found in the array, thus -1.

Sample Input 2
6

5 6 8 1 3 4

1

0

Sample Output 2
-1

Explanation 2
The element 0 is not found in the array.
    // Complete the function implementation below
    public int search(int[] nums, int target) {
             int left = 0;
        int right = nums.length - 1;
        
        while (left <= right) {
            int mid = left + (right - left) / 2;
            
            // If target found at mid
            if (nums[mid] == target) {
                return mid;
            }
            
            // Check which half is sorted
            if (nums[left] <= nums[mid]) {
                // Left half is sorted
                if (target >= nums[left] && target < nums[mid]) {
                    // Target is in left half
                    right = mid - 1;
                } else {
                    // Target is in right half
                    left = mid + 1;
                }
            } else {
                // Right half is sorted
                if (target > nums[mid] && target <= nums[right]) {
                    // Target is in right half
                    left = mid + 1;
                } else {
                    // Target is in left half
                    right = mid - 1;
                }
            }
        }
        
        return -1;
    }

divide and decrease(search space)  
- Searching in a SORTED array 
    search in a rotated sorted array
    find min in Rotated sorted  
    search in  k sorted array , merge k sorted array 
- searching with O(logN)
    Find peak Ele
    Find First & Last ele in sorted array 
- Maximise the Minimum OR Vice versa 
    koko eating bananas 
    capacity to ship packaged within D days 
    find smallest divisor given a threshold 

2 POINTER - here we consider values being pointed by the 2 pointers 
Whenever we have 2 nested for loops , think if its possible to reduce 
One loop by using two pointers  
I Both moving same direction 
II Both moving towards each other

1493 Longest sub-array of 1's After deleting one element - https://leetcode.com/problems/longest-subarray-of-1s-after-deleting-one-element/description/  
PENDING DSA - dp solution 4 this problem - space will not be O(1) the way in sliding window   
Brute Force -   
T.C. O(n) : [n] is searched by a [k] sub-array for number of subArray times i.e. k * (n - k + 1) -> k * n - k*k - k BUT k will be way to small therefore T.C. O(n*k)    
  
optimized SW solution :   
T.C. Now we just need to calci just the first window from the total number of windows i.e. (n - k + 1) - 1 = n - k where n will dominate . ' . T.C. = O(n)  
  
Intuition :   
    keep traversing the [] until the frequency of 0 increases to 2 at some idx=i . Calculate the length for the window until i -1 by removing -1(1st encountered 0)   
o number names and values of variables u will require -                                                                                                                                                                                                            left,right,zeroCount,maxLength   
Code steps 2 b kept in mind :   
2 start coding the solution :   
o first think about the purpose of vars and begin with the one whose purpose is most straight-forward -->                                                                                                                                   nums[right] == 0 zeroCount ++     
left has to be decreased when zeroCount > 2 also when   
left finds another 0 it has to decrease zero count     
right shall ++ until zeroCount <= 1 else stop   
Also   
Solution - 
            int zeroCount = 0,maxLength = 0 ,left = 0,right = 0 ; 
        while(right < nums.length){
            if(nums[right] == 0 ){
                zeroCount ++;
            }
            while(zeroCount > 1){
                if(nums[left] == 0){
                    zeroCount --;
                }
                left++;
            }
            maxLength = Math.max(maxLength,right-left+1 - zeroCount);//?
            right++;
        }
        return maxLength == nums.length ? maxLength - 1 : maxLength;

Solution : 
    public List<List<Integer>> levelOrder(TreeNode root) {
        List<List<Integer>> ans = new ArrayList<>();
        helper(root,ans,0);
        return ans;
    }
    private void helper(TreeNode node,List<List<Integer>> ans,int level){
        if(node == null) return ;
        if(level == ans.size()) ans.add(new ArrayList<>());//this one covers AL<Integer>() here  as well as ArrayList<Integer>() above 
        ans.get(level).add(node.val);        // || List<Integer> levelList = ans.get(level); levelList.add(node.val);
        helper(node.left,ans,level+1);
        helper(node.right,ans,level+1);
    }

Solution : 
    public List<List<Integer>> levelOrder(TreeNode root) {
        if(root == null) return new ArrayList<>();
        Queue<TreeNode> levelQ = new LinkedList<>();
        List<List<Integer>> ans = new ArrayList<>();
        levelQ.offer(root);
        while(!levelQ.isEmpty()){
            int levelSize = levelQ.size();
            List<Integer> currLevel=new ArrayList<>();
            for(int i = 0 ; i < levelSize ; i ++){
                TreeNode curr = levelQ.poll();
                if(curr.left != null) levelQ.offer(curr.left);
                if(curr.right != null) levelQ.offer(curr.right);
                currLevel.add(curr.val);
            }
            ans.add(currLevel);
        }   
        return ans;
    }

    Solution :  
   public List<List<Integer>> zigzagLevelOrder(TreeNode root) {
        List<List<Integer>> ans = new ArrayList<>();
        if(root == null) return ans;
        boolean reverse = false; 
        Deque <TreeNode> levelQ = new LinkedList<>();
        levelQ.offerLast(root);
        while(!levelQ.isEmpty()){
            int levelSize = levelQ.size();
            List<Integer> currLevel = new ArrayList<>();
            for(int i = 0 ; i < levelSize ; i ++){
                    if(reverse){
                TreeNode curr = levelQ.pollLast();
                    currLevel.add(curr.val);
                    if(curr.right != null) levelQ.offerFirst(curr.right);         
                    if(curr.left != null) levelQ.offerFirst(curr.left);
                    }else{
                        TreeNode curr = levelQ.pollFirst();
                        currLevel.add(curr.val);
                        if(curr.left != null) levelQ.offerLast(curr.left);                        
                        if(curr.right != null) levelQ.offerLast(curr.right);                        
                    }
            }
            reverse = ! reverse;
            ans.add(currLevel);
        }
        return ans;  
    }

    int widthOfBinaryTree(TreeNode root){
        if(root == null) return 0;
        return width(root,1,0,newArrayList<Integer>());
    }
    int width(node,level,index,leftList){
        if(root == null) return 0;
        if(level == leftList.size()) leftList.add(level);
        int leftWidth = width(node.left,level+1,index*2,leftList);
        int rightWidth = width(node.right,level+1,index*2+1,leftList);
        int maxWidth = index - leftList.get(level)  + 1;
        return Math.max(maxWidth,Math.max(leftWidth,rightWidth));
    }
Solution - 
    public int widthOfBinaryTree(TreeNode root) {
    if(root == null) return 0 ; 
    return width(root,new ArrayList<Integer>(),0,1);
    }
    private int width(TreeNode node,List<Integer> leftMostPositions,int level,int index){
        if(node == null) return 0 ;
        if(level == leftMostPositions.size()) leftMostPositions.add(index);
        int leftWidth = width(node.left,leftMostPositions,level+1,index*2);
        int rightWidth = width(node.right,leftMostPositions,level+1,index*2+1);
        int maxWidth = index - leftMostPositions.get(level) + 1 ; 
        return Math.max(maxWidth,Math.max(leftWidth,rightWidth));
    }

199 Binary Tree Right Side View  - https://leetcode.com/problems/binary-tree-right-side-view/ 
yes u know how to levelOrderT but we want the last ele from the levelList so how --->                                                                                                                                                                           poll(req Q ! dq)  the node out of levelQ then check  if(idx == levelSize 1 ) ans.add(curr.val); else .left != null offer .right != null offer  
Solution :  
    public List<Integer> rightSideView(TreeNode root) {  
        if(root == null) return new ArrayList<>(); 
        Queue<TreeNode> levelQ=new LinkedList<>();  
        List<Integer> ans = new ArrayList<>();  
        levelQ.offer(root);  
        while(!levelQ.isEmpty()){  
            int levelSize = levelQ.size();  
            for(int i = 0 ; i < levelSize ;i ++){  
                TreeNode curr = levelQ.poll();  
                if(i == levelSize - 1) ans.add(curr.val);  
                if(curr.left != null) levelQ.offer(curr.left);  
                if(curr.right != null) levelQ.offer(curr.right);   
            }  
        }  
        return ans;  
    }

116 Populating next right pointers in each node - https://leetcode.com/problems/populating-next-right-pointers-in-each-node/description/  
Means each node within a level can refer to its next right neighbor  
Naive approach PENDING DSA levelOrder traversal with S.C. O(n) cause of Queue   
Optimal approach with constant S.C.   
o how is the current node updating ? ->                                                                                                                                                                                     its not moving -y instead its +x which has a single possible mechanism  --->                                                                                                                        that is curr = curr.next ; meaning it will also operate inside a --->                                                                       while(curr != null)    
After answering the above question --->                                                                                                                                                                         If we are moving +x for curr then how are we moving down for further levels ? ---->                                                                                                                                 well its the left dfs traversal be means of Node leftMostNode = root while(leftMostNode.left !=null) leftMostNode=leftMostNode.left ;     
o basic logic to connect children of the same parent node -->                                                                                                                                                                                                               curr.left.next = curr.right  
o logic to connect rightCh of node1 to the leftCh of node2 on the same level .What's the first thing we need to do -->                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        we need to check do even have one more node on the same level whose left child needs to be pointed by next pointer of right child of the current node .Do we even have a right neighbor of the currNode ? so ->                                       if(curr.right != null){curr.right.next = curr.next.left}   
Solution : 
    public Node connect(Node root) {
        if(root == null) return null;
        Node leftMostNode = root;
        while(leftMostNode.left != null){
            Node curr = leftMostNode;
            while(curr != null){
                curr.left.next = curr.right;
                if(curr.next != null){
                    curr.right.next = curr.next.left;
                }
                curr = curr.next;
            }
            leftMostNode=leftMostNode.left;
        }
        return root;
    }
230 Kth smallest Element in a BST : https://leetcode.com/problems/kth-smallest-element-in-a-bst/

Solution : 
    public int kthSmallest(TreeNode root, int k) {
        if(root == null) return 0;
        List<Integer> inOrderList = new ArrayList<>();
        inOrder(root,inOrderList);
        return inOrderList.get(k-1);
    }
    private void inOrder(TreeNode node,List<Integer> list){
        if(node == null) return ;
        inOrder(node.left,list);
        list.add(node.val);
        inOrder(node.right,list);
    }

                private int count = 0, result = 0 ;
                public int kthSmallest(TreeNode root, int k) {
                    inOrder(root,k);
                    return result;
                }
                private void inOrder(TreeNode node,int k){
                    if(node == null) return ;
                    inOrder(node.left,k);
                    count ++;
                    if(count == k){
                        result = node.val;
                        return;
                    }
                    inOrder(node.right,k);
                }

Solution : 
        public void flatten(TreeNode root) {
            //No need to put base condition since void 
        TreeNode curr = root; 
        while(curr != null){ 
            if(curr.left != null    ){ 
            TreeNode temp = curr.left;  
            while(temp.right != null) {
                temp = temp.right ;  
            } 
        temp.right = curr.right;
        curr.right = curr.left;
        curr.left = null ;  
        } 
        curr = curr.right; 
        } 
    }

TempCode : 
    Here - 
        public void flatten(TreeNode root){

        }
Solution :
    public void flatten(TreeNode root) {
        TreeNode curr = root;
        while(curr != null){
            while(curr.left!= null){
                TreeNode temp = curr.left;
                while(temp.right != null){
                    temp = temp.right;
                }
                temp.right = curr.right ;
                curr.right = curr.left;
                curr.left = null;
            }
            curr = curr.right;
        }   
    }
PENDING DSA : 
Intuition : 
o if we look at the resulting linked list we notice that the nodes are represented in the reverse direction of the tree i.e. rightChild-> parent->leftChild . ' .
o if we invert the pointers - right pointer to the previous node and the left pointer to null it should work 
Solution : 
        public void flatten(TreeNode root) {
        helper(root,null);
    }
    private TreeNode helper(TreeNode node,TreeNode prev){
        if(node == null) return prev;
        TreeNode rightChild = helper(node.right,prev);
        TreeNode leftChild = helper(node.left,rightChild);
        node.right = leftChild;
        node.left = null;
        return node;
    }

Solution : 
    public TreeNode invertBinaryTree(TreeNode root){//One more parameter ? 
    if(root == null) return ;
    TreeNode left = invertBinaryTree(root.left);
    TreeNode right = invertBinaryTree(root.right);
    root.left = right;
    root.right = left;
    return root;
    }

236 Lowest Common ancestor of BT - https://leetcode.com/problems/lowest-common-ancestor-of-a-binary-tree/ 
BUG how many functions required u may get this wrong --->                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       1

BUG line right after nullness check -->                                                                                 if nullness check is right u will feel like there's no need for further if statements WHICH IS INDEED TRUE

LCA : the node which is located at the DEEPEST LEVEL in a tree from two given nodes . This node can itself be one of the two nodes depending on 
which one comes first. or when is null we would return root then    

Solution : 
        public TreeNode lowestCommonAncestor(TreeNode root, TreeNode p, TreeNode q) {
        if(root == null || root == p || root == q) return root;
        TreeNode leftChild = lowestCommonAncestor(root.left,p,q);
        TreeNode rightChild = lowestCommonAncestor(root.right,p,q);
        return leftChild != null && rightChild != null ? root : leftChild == null ? rightChild : leftChild;
    }

112 Path sum : optimization , may b we can consider the boolean statement root.val == targetSum when both its children are null instead of returning true straightaway     
public boolean pathSum(TreeNode root,int sum){  
            if(root == null) return false;  
        if(root.val == targetSum && root.left == null && root.right == null) return true;//  
        boolean left = hasPathSum(root.left,targetSum - root.val);   
        boolean right =  hasPathSum(root.right,targetSum - root.val);  
        return left || right; 
    }

Time Complexity : of an Algorithem Refers to relation between the size of the input it operates with and time it takes to produce the result .That is to say 
Time required by the algorithm to execute itself completely will grow quadratically as the input size changes  
Asymptotic Notation provides a concise way to describe the behavior of an algorithm's time complexity or space complexity as the input size approaches infinity. 
It allows us to focus on the growth rate of the algorithm's performance, disregarding constant factors and lower-order terms 
states that u should round off the input size to the highest power of the input size and ignore the constant  
2*n^3 + 5*n^2 + 19 Complexity ?                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              O(n^3) consider the highest power of n and ignore the constant  
(I)The Big O notation describes the worst-case scenario which is the upper-bound on the running time . 
f(n), O(g(n))  : denotes that f(n) doesn't grow faster than g(n) for sufficiently large values of n . 
Ex - If an algo has a time complexity of O(n^2) it means running time grows slower than n^2  //  
(II) Omega (GodOfWar) Notation : represents the lower bound of an algorithm's time || space complexity . It describes how the running time or space usage grows 
in the best case scenario as the input increases . 
For f(n)
(III) Theta Notation : This Asymptotyic notation represents both the uper and lower bounds of an algo's time||space . It describes how the running time of the 
algorithm grows with average-case scenario as the input size inc 
Comparison as Descending Complexity Order- O(n!) > O(2^n) > O(n^2) > O(n logn) > O(n) > O(log n),O(1) 
Space Complexity : refers to the realtion between the space a given programmes consumes at run time in the main memory AND THE input size while speaking of 
asymptotic notation

while(n>0){n=n/2 ; } log to the base 2 .Lets say n=8 then 2*2 then 4*2 so we get 2 C multiplication happening 2

O(n * log(n)) : Seen in case of sorting where we get C repeated divisions cause of being placed within a for loop . For loop has linear complexity and its body has Logarithmic 
Time grows logarithmically as the input size increases  
O(n) || Linear TC || Linear SC :Seen quite commonly in algos which iterate through the data/input just once  Running Time increases linearly

grows/changes

O(n^c) || Ploynomical TC : The running time grows at a polynomial rate with the input size. The value of "c" represents the degree of the polynomial. Higher values 
of "c" indicate worse time complexity.
O(n!) || Factorial TC The running time grows factorially with the input size. Common in algorithms that involve generating all permutations or combinations.

Crio Methodology
READ THINK AND CODE 
Milestone 1: Understand the problem clearly
1. Ask questions & clarify the problem statement clearly.
2. Take an example or two to confirm your understanding of the input/output & extend it to test cases
Milestone 2: Finalize approach & execution plan
1. Understand what type of problem you are solving.
     a. Obvious logic, tests ability to convert logic to code
     b. Figuring out logic
     c. Knowledge of specific domain or concepts
     d. Knowledge of specific algorithm
     e. Mapping real world into abstract concepts/data structures
2. Brainstorm multiple ways to solve the problem and pick one based on the TC/SC requirements 
3. Get to a point where you can explain your approach to a 10 year old 
4. Take a stab at the high-level logic & write it down. 
5. Try to offload processing to functions & keeping your main code small. 

Milestone 3: Come up with an “Instruction Manual” for a 10 year old Code by expanding your pseudocode 
1. Make sure you name the variables, functions clearly. Take a stab at the high-level logic & write it down like a detailed Instruction Manual for a 10 Year old where each line of the manual can be expanded into a logical line(s) of code. 
2. Avoid  ants in your code unless necessary; go for generic functions, you can use examples for your thinking though. Try to offload logic out of the main section as much as possible by delegating to functions
3. AVOID THIS ACCORDINGLY   Use libraries as much as possible

Milestone 4: Prove to the interviewer that your code works with unit tests Code by expanding your 10 Year Old’s "Instruction Manual” 
1. Make sure you check boundary conditions if compiler not provided dry run your code on a whiteboard or paper  
2. Discuss  Time & storage complexity AND Suggest optimizations if applicable

NOTE: Is the relation of Increasing/changing input size with the increasing/changing time consumed by our code solution  
Algorithm				Worst				Best				Avg
Bubble				O(n^2)				O(n)
Bucket					O(n^2)
Insertion 				O(n^2)			O(n)
Selection				O(n^2)			Omega(n^2)              O(n^2)

Bubble Sort | Exchange Sort | Syncing Sort
    NOTE: you forget the optimization trick HINT the way you usually get stuck at the beginning of () thinking what should come before for loop here something does come
    In-place sorting i.e. we don't copy array elements to some other tempo DS where sorting happens increasing space complexity 
    instead we sort the elements in the exact same D.S. by re-arranging them keeping space complexity constant
    Adjacent comparisons and swapping UNTIL LARGEST ELEMENT @ last or smallest element in the FIRST iteration itself.
    This process is repeated until one half of the [(since descending sorting will keep things at left)] get sorted 
    WHICH SHOULD BE AVOIDED TO improve the complexity since one section is already sorted so shouldn't be checked further
    this is done by the j iterator 
    External loop's i variable is more of a counter because jth element is not compared with ith ele instead it is compared with j-1 instead.
    i on the other hand just determines until which extent does the j iterator needs to traverse the array for comparing an element with its predecessor
    T.C. will be best case - O(n) worst case O(n square) Why because it will be n * Summation of natural numbers which is = n * ((n * (n+1)))/2; ▶️ giving n square after ignoring vars n literals for worst case scanario
        public void bubbleSort(int[] arr, int n) {
            boolean swapped;
            for (int i = 0; i < n - 1; i++) {//Because we don't need to compare the last element
                swapped = false;
                for (int j = 0; j < n - 1 - i; j++) {
                    if (arr[j] > arr[j + 1]) {// When we want descending order just keep > instead of what we have already
                        int temp = arr[j];
                        arr[j] = arr[j + 1];
                        arr[j + 1] = temp;
                        swapped = true;
                    }
                }
                if (!swapped) break; // stops early if already sorted
            }
        }

SELECTION SORT - this can also work if we put the smallest ele at first position and look for second smallest 
    o select either the max/min ele from []/ArrayList then swap it with the element where the min/max ele should have had been
    o look for max/min in the remaining []/AL section and perform the same i.e. either 1 or n-2 
    T.C. : 
        depends on the number of comparisons being made i.e. --> n-1 since last ele does not need to compared already at the correct position  
        . ' . t.c. = no. of comparisons x sum of ele ? = (n-1 )x (n-1)/2 => constants removed O(n^2) which is applicable for best,average, & worst case  
    S.C. : 
        public void selectSort(int[] arr){
        for(int i = 0 ; i < arr.length - 1;i ++){
            int min = i ; 
            for(int j = i + 1; j < arr.length ; j ++){
                if(arr[j] < arr[min]) min = j ;
            }
            int temp = arr[min];
            arr[min] = arr[i];// We are taking i over here not j because i is no longer the min/max it is j and it got updated too in the min/max var .'. we swap it with existing arr[i];
            arr[i] = temp;
        }
    }

INSERTION SORT - Starts with | which looks like square bracket .'. we dealing with sub arrays and W therefore while loop since continue swapping to the left until  
    NOTE: Bubble sort shifted the largest element to the right for ascending order 
        right array section was sorted, Insertion sort shall keep left array section as sorted. 
sort the smallest sub-array possible .length = 1 even though empty array is also sorted 
 then increase the size by 1 idx at a time by INSERTING the next ele on the right position 
 which of course means you keep swapping it with the elments on the left until the right position
    public void insertionSort(int[] arr, int n){
        for(int = 0 ; i < n  ; i ++){ // would we need i < n - 1 instead ? 
            int j = i;
            while( j > 0 && arr[j] > arr[j+1]){
                int temp = arr[j];
                arr[j] = arr[j + 1];
                arr[j + 1] = temp;
            }
        }
    }

Heapify -  
    maxHeapify() for generating a maxHeap which starts BOTTOM Up(meaning insertion from bottom) and keeps swapping the parent with child as long maxHeap property is not satisfied otherwise we have maxHeap    
    minHeapify() for generating minHeap which also starts bottom-up  and   
Insertion(binary heap has O(logn) T.C. )  - Since heapify()s are bottom up any swapping occurs from bottom n . ' . insertion happens from bottom too followed by heapify constanting swapping it until property attained !  
Deletion (binar heap has O(logn) T.C. for removing highest priority ele same for  )- root is removed and that child is brought to the root position which satisfies the maxHeap condition  
Fetching/Getting highest ele property from heap - T.C. O(1) since its the root

small_heap -> PriorityQueue<someGenerics> heap = new PriorityQueue<>(); 
large_heap -> PriorityQueue<Integer||ElseCase> heap =new PriorityQueue<>(Collections.reverseOrder()); 

o Use Min-Heap when you want the minimum element of K elements to be accessed in O(1). That is why when we want to access Kth largest element,  
    we simply push the K largest elements in the minHeap and then automatically the minimum of them will be the Kth largest, and that can be accessed in O(1) time.  
    When asked for Kth largest, use Min-Heap. 

o Use Max-Heap when you want the maximum element of K elements to be accessed in O(1). That is why when we want to access Kth smallest element, we simply push K smallest 
    elements in the maxHeap and then automatically the maximum of them will be the Kth smallest, and that can be accessed in O(1) time. When asked for Kth smallest, use 
    Max-Heap.

Find the Nth root -  problem where large number of test cases and really large input integer(although long long ) values were causing test cases to fail  
may b -  PriorityQueue<int[]> maxHeap = new PriorityQueue<>((a, b) -> b[0] - a[0]); // Max heap to store laddus count and shop index
long long power(long long x, int n) {
    if (n == 0) {
        return 1;
    }
    long long result = 1;
    while (n > 0) {
        if (n % 2 == 1) {
            result *= x;
        }
        x *= x;
        n /= 2;
    }
    return result;
}

int findNthRoot(long long X, int N) {
    if (X == 0 || N == 1) {
        return X; // Root of 0 or 1st root is the same as X
    }

    long long left = 0;
    long long right = min(X, (long long)pow(2, 30)); // Set upper bound based on X and N
    long long result = 0;

    while (left <= right) {
        long long mid = left + (right - left) / 2;

        // Calculate mid^N
        long long midPower = power(mid, N);

        if (midPower == X) {
            return mid; // Found exact root
        } else if (midPower < X) {
            result = mid;
            left = mid + 1;
        } else {
            right = mid - 1;
        }
    }

    return result;
}

int main() {
    int t;
    cin >> t;

    while (t--) {
        long long X;
        int N;
        cin >> X >> N;

        int nthRoot = findNthRoot(X, N);
        cout << nthRoot << endl;
    }

    return 0;
}

Space Optimization Tips   
o in case of dp[] it is pretty much swapping and updating values of curr , prev or temp variables   
o Keep the update-ion order of variables within the for loop from top to bottom that is update the var inside for() at the end whereas the ones declared + initialized outside for() should be updated first in FIFO manner     
o  in case of dp[][] you will have to use a temp[] which will be updated by the current[] by the end of the while loop within which curr[] was declared .

    1.Rolling State or Sliding window in general
      When current state depends on fixed number of previous states
        Solution: 
            dp[i]=dp[i]+dp[i-1]+dp[i-2];
        Questions: 
            linear recurrence relations
            fibonacci-type problems
            climibing stairs
            tribonacci
    2. Dimension reduction
        when current row depends ONLY on the previous one
        Solution: 
            dp[i][j]=dp[j];
        questions: 
            knapsack(0/1)
            subset sum
            coin change
        FIXME: Trick is to iterate backwards for (0/1) knapsack problems to avoid overwriting

tempSolution {
        int tripleJumpSolution(int n){//current number of stairs
            //base case to stop recursion if he can take 1,2 or 3 steps max then we can consider them as the smallest
            //overlapping sub problem i.e. if 1 step remains we need to return , 2-> 2(1,1 or 2 together) so 4 then 3-> (1,1,1 (2,1), (1,2) , 3) 4
            if(n==3) return 4;
            if(n==2) return 2;
            if(n==1) return 1; don't do this which means topmost will be n==0 return 1; ofcourse n<0 return 0 n if n == then n
            //my muscle memory forces me to do n-1+n-2+n-3 which doesn't seem to be entirely wrong to me since we are reducing
            //num count in each recusive call as we are moving from top to bottom i.e. biggest overlapping sub problem first then
            //gradually moving to the smallest one
            return tripleJumpSolution(n-3) + tripleJumpSolution(n-2) + tripleJumpSolution(n-1);
            //upon coming across a valid situation count that up with the next sub-problem solution with recursion
        }
        if(n<0) return 0; n==0 return 1 n == 1 or n==2 return n;
    }
Solution : -  
        //have changed the base cases and return statement for tail recursion  
        if(n <0) return 0;  
        if(n == 0 ) return 1;  
        if(n == 2 || n==1) return n;  
        return numberOfWays(n-1) + numberOfWays(n-2) + numberOfWays(n-3);  
 
Memoization
tempSolution{
    public static int tipleStepSolution(int num){
        Map<Integer<Integer> numToSolution = new hashmap<>();
        numToSolution.put(0,1);
        numToSolution.put(1,1);
        numToSolution.put(2,2);
        numToSolution.put(3,4);
        return helper(num,numToSolution);
    }
    private static int helper(int num,Map<Integer<Integer>> mapTo){
        if(mapTo.get(num)!=null) return mapTo.get(num);
        return mapTo.put(num)=helper(num-3,mapTo) + helper(num-2,mapTo) + helper(num-1,mapTo);
    }
}

    int helper(int n , int[] dp){
        if(n == 0 ) return 1;
        if(n <= 2) return n ;//what is n <<<<<<<<<<0 ?? OR what if n close to +ve infinity ? 1ev or 1 000 00 ?? or Integer.MAX_VALUE or Integer.MIN_VALUE 
        if(dp[n] != -1) return dp[n];
        return dp[n] = helper(n-3,dp) + helper(n-2,dp) + helper(n-1,dp);
    }
    int numberOfWays(int n) {
        int[] dp=new int[n+1];
        for(int i = 0 ; i < n +1 ; i ++) dp[i] = -1;
        return helper(n,dp);
    }

    public static int tripleJumpSolution(int num){
        int[] dp=new int[num+1];//Should be
        dp[0]=1;dp[1]=1;dp[2]=2;dp[3]=4;
        helper(5,dp);
        return dp[num];

    private static void helper(int num,int[] dp){
        for(int i = num ; i < dp.length ; i ++){//num-> num.length ?
            dp[i]=helper(i+1,dp) + helper(i+2,dp) + helper(i+3,dp);
        }
    }

Solution 
    int numberOfWays(int n) {
        int[] dp=new int[n+1];
        dp[0] = 1;
        dp[1] = 1;
        dp[2] = 2;
        for(int i = 3 ; i < n +1 ; i ++) {
                dp[i] = dp[i-3] + dp[i-2] + dp[i-1];
        }
        return dp[n];
    }
NOTE : one important edge case was not passing , which passed with below code :
            int numberOfWays(int n) {
          int MOD = 1000000007;
        int[] dp = new int[n + 1];
        dp[0] = 1; // Base case: 1 way to climb 0 steps

        for (int i = 1; i <= n; i++) {
            for (int j = 1; j <= 3 && j <= i; j++) {
                dp[i] = (dp[i] + dp[i - j]) % MOD;
            }
        }
        
        return dp[n];
        BELOW PASSED TOO 
       int numberOfWays(int n) {
         if (n <= 2) {
            return n;
        }
        int a = 1, b = 1, c = 2, d = 0;
        for (int i = 3; i <= n; i++) {
            d = (a + b + c) % 1000000007;
            a = b;
            b = c;
            c = d;
        }
        return d;
    }

    public int climbingStairs(int n) {
        int[] dp=new int[n+1];
        int prev2 = 1;
        int prev1 = 1;
        int curr = 0 ;// U don't need to declare curr again and again or should we ??
        for(int i = 2 ; i < n+1; i ++){
            curr = prev1 + prev2;
            prev2 = prev1 ;
            prev1 = curr;
        }
        return curr;//since curr was 0 otherwise we would have returned prev1
    }
 
    int numberOfWays(int n){
        int[] dp=new int[n+1];
        int prev2 = 1;
        int prev1 = 1;
        int prev = 2;
        for(int i = 3 ; i < n +1 ; i ++) {
                int curr = prev + prev1 + prev2;
                prev2 = prev1;
                prev1 = prev;
                prev = curr;
        }
        return prev;
    }

Solution :
       public static int ninjaTraining(int n, int points[][]) {
         return maxMeritPointsHelper(points, n, 0, -1);}

    public static int maxMeritPointsHelper(int[][] points, int n, int day, int prevActivity) {
        if (day == n) {
            return 0;
        }

        int maxPoints = Integer.MIN_VALUE;
        for (int activity = 0; activity < 3; activity++) {
            if (activity != prevActivity) {
                int pointsToday = points[day][activity];
                int pointsAfterToday = maxMeritPointsHelper(points, n, day + 1, activity);
                maxPoints = Math.max(maxPoints, pointsToday + pointsAfterToday);
            }
        }
        return maxPoints;
    }

Complete tabulation Solution 
public static int ninjaTraining(int n, int points[][]) {
        int[][] dp=new int[n][4];//Paste
        for(int i = 0 ; i < n ; i ++){//sensible ?? with default value of int as 0 as it is ?? 
            for(int j = 0 ; j < 4 ; j ++){
                dp[i][j] = 0;
            }
        }
        dp[0][0] = Math.max(points[0][1],points[0][2]);
        dp[0][1] = Math.max(points[0][0],points[0][2]);
        dp[0][2] = Math.max(points[0][0],points[0][1]);
        dp[0][3] = Math.max(points[0][1],Math.max(points[0][1],points[0][2]));
        for(int day = 1; day<n; day++){
            for(int last = 0 ; last < 4 ; last++){
                dp[day][last] = 0 ;
                for(int task = 0 ; task < 3 ; task ++){
                    if(task != last){
                        int point = points[day][task] + dp[day-1][task];
                        dp[day][last]=Math.max(dp[day][last],point);
                    }
                }
            }
        }
        return dp[n-1][3];
        // Write your code here..
    }

we will start by initializing the array with what we had initialized the matrix

    public int uniquePaths(int m, int n) {
        //below is a waste of time helper() takes care of these cases anyway besides empty grid is not even a case 
        //Just ask the interviewer or look at the constraints of row and col its A DP TIP 
        // Base condition which can b included the way root == null return null : -  
            if(m == 0 && n == 0) return 0;
            if(m == 1 && n == 1) return 1;
        return helper(m,0,n,0);        
    }
    private int helper(int m , int row ,int n , int col){
        if(row >= m || col >= n) return 0;
        if(row == m-1 && col == n-1) return 1;//It worked fine with || which is right too cause if hidden test case includes row=5 and col = 0 then || great !
        return helper(m,row+1,n,col) + helper(m,row,n,col+1);
    }

Solution : 
    public int uniquePaths(int m, int n) {
        if(m == 0 && n == 0)return 1;
        int[][] memo=new int[m+1][n+1];
        for(int i = 0 ; i <= m ; i ++){
            for(int j = 0 ;j <= n ; j ++) memo[i][j] = -1;
        }       
        return helper(m,1,n,1,memo);
    }
    private int helper(int m , int row , int n , int col,int[][] memo){
        if(row > m || col > n) return 0;
        if(memo[row][col] != -1) return memo[row][col];
        if(row ==  m || col == n) return 1;
        int right = helper(m,row+1,n,col,memo);
        int down = helper(m,row,n,col+1,memo);
        return memo[row][col]=right+down;// u can avoid using 1 000 000 007
    }

Solution : 
    leetcode sol 
          if(m == 0 && n == 0)return 1;
        int[][] dp=new int[m+1][n+1];
        for(int i =0 ; i < m + 1 ; i ++){
            for(int j = 0 ;j < n + 1 ; j ++){
                dp[0][j] = 1;
                dp[i][0] = 1;
            }
        }
        for(int i = 1 ; i < m + 1 ; i ++ ){
            for(int j = 1 ; j < n + 1 ; j ++){
                if(i == m || j == n){
                dp[i][j] =  dp[i-1][j-1];
                }else{
                    dp[i][j] = dp[i-1][j] + dp[i][j-1];// u can avoid 1e9 -> 787 i.e. 8 zeros then 7
                }
            }
        }
        return dp[m][n];
        }
    public int uniquePaths(int m, int n) {
        if(m == 0 && n == 0) return 0;
        if(m == 1 && n == 1) return 1;
        int[][] memo=new int[m][n];
        for(int i =0 ; i < m ;i ++){
            for(int j = 0 ; j < n ; j ++){
                memo[i][0] = 1;
                memo[0][j] = 1;
            }
        }
        for(int i = 1 ; i < m ; i ++){
            for(int j = 1 ;j < n ;j ++){
                memo[i][j] = (memo[i-1][j] + memo[i][j-1])%1000000007;
            }
        }
    return memo[m-1][n-1];
    }
