Solution :  
        public int uniquePaths(int m, int n) { 
        int[] dp=new int[Math.min(m,n)]; 
        for(int i = 0 ; i < dp.length ; i ++){ 
            dp[i]=1; 
        } 
        int mod = 1000000007;//Some huge test cases would have not passed without this   
        for(int i =1 ; i < (m > n ? m:n) ; i ++){ 
                int prev = 1;  
            for(int j = 1 ; j <(m>n? n :m) ; j ++){  
                dp[j] =(dp[j] + prev)%mod; 
                prev = dp[j]; 
            }   
             
        }  
        return dp[Math.min(m-1,n-1)]; 
        } 
 
return dp[n - 1];

Solution : 
    public int findTargetSumWays(int[] nums, int target) {
        //u can ignore below two conditions and call ways straightaway 
        //Its just that I got used to it cause of dp and tree questions 
       if(nums.length == 0) return 0 ; 
       if(nums.length == 1){
            if(nums[0] == target){
                return 1;
            }else{
                return 0;
            }
       }
        return ways(nums,target,0,0);
       }
       private int ways(int[] nums,int target,int idx , int currS){
        if(idx >= nums.length){
            if( idx > nums.length ){ 
                return 0;
            }else if(currS == target){
                return 1;
            }else{
                return 0;
            }
        }
        int addSolution = ways(nums,target,idx+1,currS + nums[idx]); 
        int subsSolution = ways(nums,target,idx+1,currS - nums[idx]); 
        return addSolution + subsSolution;
       }

    public int findTargetSumWays(int[] nums, int target) {
     if(nums.length <= 0 ) return 0 ; 
     int sum = 0 ; 
    for(int eachEle : nums) sum += eachEle;
    if(target > Math.abs(sum)) return 0;
    int[][] memo = new int[nums.length+1][target+2001];
    for(int i = 0 ; i < nums.length + 1 ; i ++){
        for(int j= 0 ;j < target+2001 ; j ++){
            memo[i][j] = Integer.MIN_VALUE;
        }
    }
     return sumWays(nums,0,target,memo);
    }
    private int sumWays(int []nums,int i , int sum,int[][] memo){
        if(i >= nums.length){
            if(i > nums.length){
                return 0 ;
            }else if(sum == 0){
                return memo[i][sum+1000]=1;
            }else {
                return 0 ;
            }
        }
        if(memo[i][sum+1000] != Integer.MIN_VALUE) return memo[i][sum+1000];
        int addEle = sumWays(nums,i+1,sum+nums[i],memo);// as such no. of sum ways 
        int substractEle = sumWays(nums,i+1,sum-nums[i],memo);//as such no. of substract ways 
        return memo[i][sum+1000] = addEle + substractEle ; 
    }

Solution :    
        static boolean subsetSum(int a[], int sum){
        return helper(a,sum,0);
    }
    private static boolean helper(int[] a,int sum,int i){
        if(i >= a.length || sum < 0) return false;
        if(sum == 0) return true;
        boolean pick = helper(a,sum-a[i],i+1);
        boolean not_pick = helper(a,sum,i+1);
        return pick || not_pick ;
    }

    private static int helper(int a[],int sum,int idx,int[][] memo){ 
        if(idx == a.length || sum < 0) return 0; 
        if(memo[sum][idx] != -1) return memo[sum][idx]; 
        if(sum == 0) return  1 ;  
        int include = helper(a,sum-a[idx],idx+1,memo); 
        int exclude = helper(a,sum,idx+1,memo); 
        boolean ans = include == 1 || exclude == 1 ; 
        return ans == true ? 1 : 0;
    }
Memoization with boolean memo[] curr with indexOutOfBounds :  
    static boolean subsetSum(int a[], int sum){
        boolean[][] memo=new boolean[a.length + 1][sum+1];
        return helper(a,sum,0,memo);
    }
    private static boolean helper(int[] a,int sum,int i,boolean[][] memo){
        if(i > a.length || sum < 0) return false;
        if(memo[i][sum] != false) return memo[i][sum];
        if(sum == 0) return true;
        boolean pick = helper(a,sum-a[i],i+1,memo);
        boolean not_pick = helper(a,sum,i+1,memo);
        return pick || not_pick ;
    }

Solution : 
        static boolean subsetSum(int a[], int sum){
        int n = a.length;
         boolean[][] dp = new boolean[n + 1][sum + 1];
    
    // Base case: If the target sum is 0, it's always possible to achieve it with an empty subset
    for (int i = 0; i <= n; i++) {
        dp[i][0] = true;
    }
    
    // Fill the dp array using dynamic programming
    for (int i = 1; i <= n; i++) {
        for (int j = 1; j <= sum; j++) {
            // If the current number is greater than the current sum, skip it
            if (a[i - 1] > j) {
                dp[i][j] = dp[i - 1][j];
            } else {
                // Take the maximum of including and excluding the current number
                dp[i][j] = dp[i - 1][j] || dp[i - 1][j - a[i - 1]];
            }
        }
    }
    
    // Return whether it's possible to achieve the target sum
    return dp[n][sum];

Array subset sum equals K - https://www.techiedelight.com/subset-sum-problem/
public static boolean subsetSum(int[] A, int n, int k){
    if(n == 1 && a[0] == k) return true;
    if(n == 1 && a[0] != k) return false;
     int ans = helper(A,k,0);
}
private int helper(int[] a,int k,int idx){
    if(idx >= a.length) return false;
    if(a[idx] == k) return true;
    int include = a[idx] + helper(a,k,idx+1);)
    int exclude =  helper(a,k,idx+1);
    if(include == k || exclude ==k) return include ;
}

Solution : 
        public int numDecodings(String s) {
        if(s == null || s.length() == 0) return 0 ;
        return helper(s,0);
    }
    private int helper(String s,int idx){
        if(idx == s.length()) return 1;
        if(s.charAt(idx) == '0') return 0;
        int ways = helper(s,idx+1);
        if(idx + 1 < s.length()  && Integer.parseInt(s.substring(idx,idx+2))<=26){
            ways += helper(s,idx+2);
        }
        return ways ;
    }

Solution : 
    public int numDecodings(String s) {
        if(s == null || s.length() == 0) return 0 ;
        int[] dp=new int[s.length()];
        for(int i = 0 ; i < dp.length ; i ++){
            dp[i]=-1;
        }
        return helper(s,0,dp);
    }
    private int helper(String s,int idx,int[] dp){
        if(idx == s.length() ) return 1;
        if(dp[idx] != -1) return dp[idx] ;
        if(s.charAt(idx) == '0') return 0;
        int ways = helper(s,idx+1,dp);
        if(idx + 1 < s.length()  && Integer.parseInt(s.substring(idx,idx+2))<=26){
            ways += helper(s,idx+2,dp);
        }
        return dp[idx] = ways ;
    }

Solution : 
        public int numDecodings(String s) {
         int n = s.length();
        if (n == 0 || s.charAt(0) == '0') {
            return 0;
        }

        int[] dp = new int[n + 1];
        dp[0] = 1;
        dp[1] = (s.charAt(0) == '0') ? 0 : 1;
    //            int mod = 1000000007;Got submitted fine without mod unlike CRIO 
        for (int i = 2; i <= n; i++) {
            int oneDigit = Integer.parseInt(s.substring(i - 1, i));
            int twoDigits = Integer.parseInt(s.substring(i - 2, i));
            if (oneDigit >= 1) {
    //                dp[i] = (dp[i] + dp[i - 1]) % 1000000007;
                dp[i] = (dp[i] + dp[i - 1]) ;
            }
            if (twoDigits >= 10 && twoDigits <= 26) {
    //                dp[i] = (dp[i] + dp[i - 2]) % 1000000007;
                dp[i] = (dp[i] + dp[i - 2]);
            }
        }

        return dp[n];
    }

Question Find a path for the robot in a grid DIFF : 
Imagine a robot sitting in the upper left corner of a grid with R rows and C columns. The robot can only move in two directions, right and down. Certain cells are "off limits" such that the robot cannot step on them. Find a path for the robot from the top left to the bottom right.

Input format
    First line will contain two space separated integers N and M, where N denotes the number of rows and M denotes the number of columns in the grid, respectively.

    Next N lines will have M space separated integers which represent the grid. A 0 value means the robot can enter this cell and 1 value means this cell is blocked.

    Output format
    Print the path from (1,1) to (N,M) that the robot can take.

    On each line, print the Row and Col numbers of the cell, separated by space which the robot next goes to, along its path. The numbering for Rows and Columns start from 1, not 0.

    Print 'Not Possible' if there is no path to reach (N,M) from (1,1)

    Note: There could be multiple correct paths, any one path can be specified.
Solution with 1 edge test case failing :  
      private boolean canMove(int[][] grid, int row, int col, int n, int m, boolean[][] visited) {
        return (row >= 0 && row < n && col >= 0 && col < m && grid[row][col] == 0 && !visited[row][col]);
    }

    // Recursive function to find the path using Depth First Search (DFS)
    private boolean findPath(int[][] grid, int row, int col, int n, int m, boolean[][] visited, List<String> path) {
        if (row == n - 1 && col == m - 1) {
            path.add((row + 1) + " " + (col + 1));
            return true;
        }

        if (canMove(grid, row, col, n, m, visited)) {
            visited[row][col] = true;
            path.add((row + 1) + " " + (col + 1));

            if (findPath(grid, row + 1, col, n, m, visited, path) || findPath(grid, row, col + 1, n, m, visited, path)) {
                return true;
            }

            path.remove(path.size() - 1);
        }

        return false;
    }

    // Main function to find the path for the robot
    Vector<String> robotInAGrid(int grid[][], int n, int m) {
        List<String> path = new ArrayList<>();
        boolean[][] visited = new boolean[n][m];

        if (findPath(grid, 0, 0, n, m, visited, path)) {
            Vector<String> result = new Vector<>();
            result.addAll(path);
            return result;
        } else {
            Vector<String> result = new Vector<>();
            result.add("Not Possible");
            return result;
        }
    }

Target Sum : 
You are given an integer array nums and an integer target.

You want to build an expression out of nums by adding one of the symbols '+' and '-' before each integer in nums 
and then concatenate all the integers.
For example, if nums = [2, 1], you can add a '+' before 2 and a '-' before 1 and concatenate them to build 
the expression "+2-1".
Return the number of different expressions that you can build, which evaluates to target.
Input format
First line of input contains 2 integers, n and target denoting the number of elements in the integer array and the target to be achieved.

The next n lines contain the n elements of the integer array.

Output format
Return the number of different expressions that you can build, which evaluates to target.
Solution which passed it : 
     static int targetSum(int[] nums,int target){
   Map<String, Integer> memo = new HashMap<>();
        return calculateWays(nums, 0, 0, target, memo);
    }

    static int calculateWays(int[] nums, int index, int sum, int target, Map<String, Integer> memo) {
        if (index == nums.length) {
            return (sum == target) ? 1 : 0;
        }

        String key = index + "," + sum;
        if (memo.containsKey(key)) {
            return memo.get(key);
        }

        int currentNumber = nums[index];
        int waysFromAddition = calculateWays(nums, index + 1, sum + currentNumber, target, memo);
        int waysFromSubtraction = calculateWays(nums, index + 1, sum - currentNumber, target, memo);

        memo.put(key, waysFromAddition + waysFromSubtraction);
        return memo.get(key);
    }

Solution without Tail recursion : 
public int longestCommonSubsequence(String text1, String text2) {
      if(text1 == null || text2 == null || text1.isEmpty() || text2.isEmpty()) return 0;
      return subSequence(text1,0,text2,0);  
    }
    private int subSequence(String s1,int s1I,String s2,int s2I){
        if(s1I >= s1.length() || s2I >= s2.length()) return 0;
        if(s1.charAt(s1I) == s2.charAt(s2I)){
            return 1 + subSequence(s1,s1I+1,s2,s2I+1);
        }
        int incS1 = subSequence(s1,s1I+1,s2,s2I);
        int incS2 = subSequence(s1,s1I,s2,s2I+1);
        return Math.max(incS1,incS2); 
    }
Solution with Tail Recursion - 

      public int longestCommonSubsequence(String text1, String text2) {
        return lcs(text1, text2, text1.length(), text2.length());
    }

    private int lcs(String text1, String text2, int m, int n) {
        if (m == 0 || n == 0) {
            return 0;
        } else if (text1.charAt(m - 1) == text2.charAt(n - 1)) {
            return 1 + lcs(text1, text2, m - 1, n - 1);
        } else {
            return Math.max(lcs(text1, text2, m, n - 1), lcs(text1, text2, m - 1, n));
        }
    }

SolutionI - 
    public int longestCommonSubsequence(String text1, String text2) {
      if(text1 == null || text2 == null || text1.isEmpty() || text2.isEmpty()) return 0;
      int[][] memo=new int[text1.length() ][text2.length() ];
        for(int i = 0 ;i < memo.length ; i ++) Arrays.fill(memo[i],-1);
      return subSequence(text1,0,text2,0,memo);  
    }
    private int subSequence(String s1,int s1I,String s2,int s2I,int[][] memo){
        if(s1I >= s1.length() || s2I >= s2.length()) return 0;
        if(memo[s1I][s2I] != -1) return memo[s1I][s2I] ;
        if(s1.charAt(s1I) == s2.charAt(s2I)){
            return 1 + subSequence(s1,s1I+1,s2,s2I+1,memo);
        }
        int incS1 = subSequence(s1,s1I+1,s2,s2I,memo);
        int incS2 = subSequence(s1,s1I,s2,s2I+1,memo);
        return memo[s1I][s2I]=Math.max(incS1,incS2); 
    }    
SolutionII - 

    public int longestCommonSubsequence(String text1, String text2) {
        int m = text1.length();
        int n = text2.length();
        int[][] dp=new int[m+1][n+1];
        for(int i = 0 ; i < m ; i ++){
            for(int j = 0 ; j < n ; j ++){
                dp[i][j]=-1;
            }
        }
        return helper(text1,m,0,text2,n,0,dp);
    }
    private int helper(String s1,int m,int i,String s2,int n,int j){
        if(i == m || j == n) return 0;
        if(dp[i][j] != -1) return dp[i][j];
        if(s1.charAt(i) == s2.charAt(j)){
            return dp[i][j] = 1 + helper(s1,m,i+1,s2,n,j+1);
        }else{
            return dp[i][j] = Math.max(helper(s1,m,i+1,s2,n,j),helper(s1,m,i,s2,n,j+1));
        }
    }

   public int longestCommonSubsequence(String text1, String text2) {
        int m = text1.length();
        int n = text2.length();
        int[][] dp=new int[m+1][n+1];
        for(int i = 1 ; i < m+1 ; i ++){
            for(int j = 1 ; j < n+1 ; j ++){
                if(text1.charAt(i-1) == text2.charAt(j-1)) {
                dp[i][j] = 1 + dp[i-1][j-1];
                }else{
                    dp[i][j] = Math.max(dp[i-1][j],dp[i][j-1]);
                }
            }
        }
     return dp[m][n];
    }

Correct Space Optimized Solution : {
public static int longestCommonSubsequence(String s, String t) {
    int n = s.length();
    int m = t.length();
    int[] prev = new int[m + 1];
    int[] curr = new int[m + 1];
    
    for (int j = 0; j <= m; j++) {
        prev[j] = 0;
    }
    
    for (int i = 0; i <= n; i++) {
        curr[0] = 0;
    }
    
    for (int i = 1; i <= n; i++) {
        for (int j = 1; j <= m; j++) {
            if (s.charAt(i - 1) == t.charAt(j - 1)) {
                curr[j] = 1 + prev[j - 1];
            } else {
                curr[j] = Math.max(prev[j], curr[j - 1]);
            }
        }
        System.arraycopy(curr, 0, prev, 0, m + 1);
    }
    return curr[m];
}
}

   public static int longestCommonSubsequence(String s, String t) {
    int n = s.length();
    int m = t.length();

    for (int j = 0; j <= m; j++) {
        prev[j] = 0;//will b filled below

    for (int i = 0; i <= n; i++) {
        curr[0] = 0;//will be filled below

                    tempi++; 
                    tempj++; 
                    ans ++; 
                }

            result = Math.max(result, compute(s1, s1Length, i + 1, s2, s2Length, j));
            result = Math.max(result, compute(s1, s1Length, i, s2, s2Length, j + 1));
            return result;

        static int longestCommonSubstring(String s1, String s2){
        int s1Size = s1.length();
        int s2Size = s2.length(); 
        int[][] dp=new int[s1Size+1][s2Size+1]; //Even if you leave the +1 n keept it instead as s1SizeXs2Size it will still b fine , u may include +1 case in ur tabulation solution instead 
        for(int i = 0 ; i < s1Size + 1 ; i ++){//use 2 nested loops  
            Arrays.fill(dp[i],-1); 
        } 
        return helper(s1,s1Size,0,s2,s2Size,0,dp); 
    } 
    private static int helper(String s1,int s1Size,int s1Idx,String s2,int s2Size , int s2Idx,int[][] dp){  
 
        if(s1Idx >= s1Size || s2Idx >= s2Size) return 0;  
        if(dp[s1Idx][s2Idx] != - 1) return dp[s1Idx][s2Idx]; 
        int result = 0 ; 
        if(s1.charAt(s1Idx) == s2.charAt(s2Idx)){  
            int ans = 1 ;//long constraints check    
            int s1Inc = s1Idx + 1; 
            int s2Inc = s2Idx + 1; 
            while(s1Inc < s1Size && s2Inc < s2Size &&s1.charAt(s1Inc) == s2.charAt(s2Inc)){ 
                s1Inc++; 
                s2Inc++; 
                ans++; 
            } 
            result= ans; 
        } 
            result = Math.max(result,helper(s1,s1Size,s1Idx+1,s2,s2Size,s2Idx,dp)); 
             result = Math.max(result,helper(s1,s1Size,s1Idx,s2,s2Size,s2Idx+1,dp)); 
             dp[s1Idx][s2Idx]=result; 
        return result; 
    }

Solution : 
    static int longestCommonSubstring(String s1, String s2){
    int s1Length = s1.length();
    int s2Length = s2.length();
    int maxLength = 0 ;
    int[] dp=new int[s2Length+1];
    for(int i=1;i<=s1Length;i++){
        int prev= 0;
        for(int j = 1 ;j <= s2Length; j ++){
            int temp = dp[j];
            if(s1.charAt(i-1) == s2.charAt(j-1)){
                dp[j] = 1 + prev;
                maxLength = Math.max(maxLength,dp[j]);
            }else{
                dp[j] = 0 ;
            }
            prev = temp;
        }

    }
    return maxLength;
}

    static int longestCommonSubstring(String s1, String s2){//Correct tabulation 

        int n = s1.length(); 
        int m = s2.length();
        int[][] dp=new int[n+1][m+1];
        for(int i = 0 ; i < n+1 ; i ++){
            for(int j = 0 ; j < m +1 ; j ++){
                dp[i][0]=0;
                dp[0][j]=0; 
            } 
        } 
        int ans = 0 ; 
        for(int i = 1 ; i < n+1 ; i ++){//i = n-1 ?  
            for(int j = 1; j < m +1 ; j ++){ 
                if(s1.charAt(i-1) == s2.charAt(j-1)){ 
                    dp[i][j]= 1 + dp[i-1][j-1];  
                    ans = Math.max(ans,dp[i][j]); 
                }else{ 
                    dp[i][j] = 0; 
                } 
            } 
        } 
        return ans; 
    }

Solution : 
        int s1Length = s1.length();
    int s2Length = s2.length();
    int[] dp = new int[s2Length + 1];
    int maxLength = 0;
    
    // DP iteration
    for (int i = 1; i <= s1Length; i++) {
        int prev = 0; // Store the value of dp[i-1][j-1]
        for (int j = 1; j <= s2Length; j++) {
            int temp = dp[j]; // Store the value of dp[i-1][j]
            if (s1.charAt(i - 1) == s2.charAt(j - 1)) {
                dp[j] = 1 + prev; // Update dp[i][j]
                maxLength = Math.max(maxLength, dp[j]);
            } else {
                dp[j] = 0; // Reset dp[i][j] because characters don't match
            }
            prev = temp; // Update prev for the next iteration
        }
    }
    return maxLength;

private String Substrings(String s,int beginInd,int endInd){ 
    if(beginInd>endInd || beginInd < 0 || endInd > s.length) { 
        throw new IllegalArgumentException("Invalid indices"); 
    }  
    char[] result = new char[endInd-beginInd]; 
    for(int i = 0 ; i < endInd - beginInd ; i++) { 
        result[i]=s.charAt(i + beginInd); 
    } 
    return new String(result); 
}

Solution  
      if (n <= 0) { 
            return 0; // Base case: No steps or negative steps, no way to climb 
            // But what when n's value is way way less than 0 ? Ask interviewer or seek guidance from the question 
            //Use Integer.MIN_VALUE;
            //Also when value returned from the function is way way more than n besides it is close to the positive infinity then use 
            //User Integer.MAX_VALUE; 
            //In both cases we initialize or use these extreme values which certaingly can't be compatible with our exising code 
            //But then what's 1ev ?? 
        } else if (n == 1) { 
            return 1; // Base case: Only one step, one way to climb (1 step)  
        } 

        // Create an array to store the number of ways to reach each step
        int[] dp = new int[n + 1];

        // Initialize base cases
        dp[0] = 1; // 0 steps (base case), there is 1 way: not taking any steps
        dp[1] = 1; // 1 step (base case), there is 1 way: taking 1 step
        dp[2] = 2; // 2 steps, there are 2 ways: (1+1 step) or (2 steps)
        
        // Calculate the number of ways to reach each step using dynamic programming
        for (int i = 3; i <= n; i++) {
            // The number of ways to reach step i is the sum of the number of ways to reach steps (i-1), (i-2), and (i-3)
            dp[i] = dp[i - 1] + dp[i - 2] + dp[i - 3];
        }

        // The final answer is stored in dp[n], which represents the number of ways to reach the nth step
        return dp[n];


PERMUATION DYNAMIC PROGRAMMING PROBLEMS
NOTE java reverse() : T.C. O(n)  
o Traverses the list once ,  
o calculates the middle index  
o  swaps the symmetrically opposite elements  
.reverse(List<T> list){ 
    int size = list.size(); 
    int mid = size/2; 
    for(int i = 0 ; i < mid ; i++){ 
        int oppositeEleIndex = size -i -1; 
        swap(list,i,oppositeEleIndex); 
    } 
} 
void swap(List<T> list,int i,intj ){ 
    temp T = list.get(i); 
    list.set(i,list.get(j)); 
    list.set(j,T); 
} 
I Linear O(n) S.C O(n) 
s1 : given in the question  
s2 = s1.reverse();

    public String longestPalindrome(String s) { 
        if(s == null || s.isEmpty()) return "";
        return recursivePalindrome(s,0,s.length()-1);
    }
    private String recursivePalindrome(String s,int start,int end){
        if(start > end) return "";
        if(start == end) return s.substring(start,end+1);
        if(s.charAt(start) == s.charAt(end)){
            String middleString = recursivePalindrome(s,start+1,end-1);
            if(middleString.length() == end - start - 1){
                return s.charAt(start) + middleString + s.charAt(end);
            }
        }
        String startInc = recursivePalindrome(s,start+1,end);
        String endDec = recursivePalindrome(s,start,end-1);
        return startInc.length() > endDec.length() ? startInc : endDec;
        }

Solution  forget this one : 
    public  String  longestPalindrome(String s){
            if (s == null || s.length() == 0) return "";
        memo = new HashMap<>();
        return findLongestPalindrome(s, 0, s.length() - 1,memo);
    }

    private String findLongestPalindrome(String s, int start, int end) {
        if (start > end) {
            return "";
        }
        if (start == end) {
            return s.substring(start, start + 1);
        }
        String key = start + "," + end;
        if (memo.containsKey(key)) {
            return memo.get(key);
        }
        if (s.charAt(start) == s.charAt(end)) {
            String innerSubstring = findLongestPalindrome(s, start + 1, end - 1);
            if (innerSubstring.length() == (end - start - 1)) {
                String result = s.charAt(start) + innerSubstring + s.charAt(end);
                memo.put(key, result);
                return result;
            }
        }
        String option1 = findLongestPalindrome(s, start + 1, end);
        String option2 = findLongestPalindrome(s, start, end - 1);
        String result = option1.length() > option2.length() ? option1 : option2;
        memo.put(key, result);
        return result;
    }

     static int longestPalindromicSubstringLength(String str) {
        int n = str.length();
        int ans = 1;
    for(int i = 0 ; i < n ; i ++){
        int tempLen = 1 ; 
        int left = i - 1; 
        int right = i + 1;
        while(left>= 0 && right <= n-1 && str.charAt(left) == str.charAt(right)){
            tempLen += 2 ; left -- ; right ++;
        }
        ans = Math.max(ans,tempLen);
    }
    //Even 
    for(int i = 0 ; i < n ;i ++){
        int tempLenEven = 2 ; 
        if(str.charAt(i) == str.charAt(i+1))
        int left = i -1 ; 
        int right = i + 2;
        int result = 1;
        while(left >= 0 && right <= n - 1 && str.charAt(left) == str.charAt(right)){
            tempLenEven += 2 ; left --; right ++;
        }
        result=Math.max(result,tempLenEven);
    }
    return Math.max(result,ans);
    }

FRACTIONAL KNAP SACK : use greedy approach , most valuable SUBSET item with a total value of EQUAL to the weight W(capacity)
given the weights & values of N items put inside a knapsack of W capacity we can break items'(weight ? not sure) to maximize total value of the knapsack  
in fractions , floating points 

O/1  KNAP-SACK PROBLEM : dynamic programming , gets most valuable SUBSET item with a total value of LESS THAN <= total weight W(capacity)
given N items with inidividual wi weights and values vi each BUT the bag of W capacity is EMPTY at first . 
Target is to either pick or not pick such that sum of the associated values vi is maximum

Solution : 
        static long maxValue(long W, long wt[], long val[],int index , int n){
        if(index == n || W == 0) return 0; 
        long not_pick= maxValue(W,wt,val,index+1,n); 
        long pick = Integer.MIN_VALUE ;//Works fine with minus  -100000000 too 
        if(W >= wt[index]){ 
            pick = val[index] + maxValue(W-wt[index],wt,val,index+1,n); 
        } 
        return Math.max(pick,not_pick); 
        }

	public static int maximumNonAdjacentSum(ArrayList<Integer> nums) {
		return helper(nums,0);
	}
	public static int helper(ArrayList<Integer> nums,int idx ){
		if(idx >= nums.size()) return 0;
		int pick = helper(nums,idx+2) + nums.get(idx); 
		int not_pick = helper(nums,idx+1) + 0 ;
		return Math.max(pick,not_pick);
	}

Solution : 
	public static int maximumNonAdjacentSum(ArrayList<Integer> nums) {
	  int[] memo = new int[nums.size()];
	for(int i = 0  ; i < nums.size() ; i ++){
		memo[i] = -1;
	}
    return helper(nums, 0, memo);
    }

    public static int helper(ArrayList<Integer> nums, int idx, int[] memo) {
    if (idx >= nums.size()) return 0;
    if (memo[idx] != -1) return memo[idx]; // Return memoized result if available

    int pick = helper(nums, idx + 2, memo) + nums.get(idx); 
    int not_pick = helper(nums, idx + 1, memo);
    return memo[idx] = Math.max(pick, not_pick);
    }

    public static int maximumNonAdjacentSum(ArrayList<Integer> nums) {
	  int[] dp = new int[nums.size()];
	  if(nums.size() == 0) return 0 ; 
     dp[0] = nums.get(0); 
	  if(nums.size()>1)  dp[1] = Math.max(nums.get(0),nums.get(1));
	for(int i = 2  ; i < nums.size() ; i ++){
		int pick = nums.get(i) + dp[i-2];
        int not_pick = dp[i-1]; 
        dp[i] = Math.max(pick, not_pick);
	}
  return dp[nums.size()-1];
    }

Solution : 
    public static int maximumNonAdjacentSum(ArrayList<Integer> nums) {
		if(nums.size() == 0) return 0 ; 
     	int prev2 = 0 ;  
		int prev1 = nums.get(0); 
	   for(int i = 1 ; i < nums.size() ; i ++){ 
	   int curr = Math.max(prev2+nums.get(i), prev1);
	   prev2 = prev1; 
	   prev1 = curr;
	   }
	return prev1;
	}

            public int rob(int[] nums) {
        int n = nums.length;
        return helper(nums,n,0);
            }
        private int helper(int[] nums,int n,int idx){
        if(idx >= n) return 0;
        int leaveHouse = helper(nums,n,idx+1);
        int robHouse = nums[idx] + helper(nums,n,idx+2);
        return Math.max(leaveHouse,robHouse); 
        }
        public static long houseThief(int n, int[] arr) {
        return helper(arr, n - 1, 0, 0);
        }

    private static long helper(int[] arr, int pos, long prevRobbed, long prevNotRobbed) {
    if (pos < 0) {
        return prevRobbed;  // Return maximum when reaching the end
    }

    long rob = arr[pos] + prevNotRobbed;  // Current house value + not robbing previous
    long notRob = Math.max(prevRobbed, prevNotRobbed);  // Max of robbing or not robbing previously

    return helper(arr, pos - 1, rob, notRob);  // Recursive call with updated values
    }

Solution : 
        public int rob(int[] nums) {
            if(nums == null || nums.length == 0) return 0;
            if(nums.length == 1) return nums[0];
            int n = nums.length;
            int[] dp = new int[n+1];
            for(int i = 0 ; i < n+1 ; i ++){
                dp[i]= -1;
            }
        return helper(nums,n,0,dp);
    }
    private int helper(int[] nums,int n,int idx,int[] dp){
        if(idx >= n) return 0;
        if( dp[idx] != -1) return dp[idx];
        int leaveHouse = helper(nums,n,idx+1,dp);
        int robHouse = nums[idx] + helper(nums,n,idx+2,dp);
        return dp[idx] = Math.max(leaveHouse,robHouse); 
    }

   public int rob(int[] nums) {
        if (nums == null || nums.length == 0) return 0;
        if (nums.length == 1) return nums[0];

        int[] dp = new int[nums.length];
        dp[0] = nums[0];
        dp[1] = Math.max(nums[0], nums[1]);

        for (int i = 2; i < nums.length; i++) {
            dp[i] = Math.max(dp[i - 1], nums[i] + dp[i - 2]);
        }
        return dp[nums.length - 1];
    }

Space Optimization :
BUG how u calci curr ? u usually make bugs here -->                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         u forget to add nums[i]                         -->                                                                                                                 int curr = Math.max(prev1,nums[i] + prev2);
BUG How are we updating the  prev2 (since it occurs twice before curr)  prev1 (since it occurs RIGHT before curr ) ; and                                                                                                                                                          u were updating prev1 first which is wrong                                                                                                                                                        Top to bottom , above var becomes below var i.e. prev2 becomes prev1 while prev1 becomes curr  
o remember to remove the dp array otherwise space shall still be O(n);
o known value that occurs 2 positions before the first unknown value                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         When no houses to rob , theft = 0 i.e. prev2 = 0 ;
o known value that occurs 1 position before the first unknown value                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           When 1 house to rob , then rob it that is prev1 =  nums[0]; 
Solution :
    public int rob(int[] nums) { 
        if (nums == null || nums.length == 0) return 0;
        if (nums.length == 1) return nums[0];
        int[] dp = new int[nums.length];
        int prev2 = nums[0];
        int prev1 = Math.max(nums[0], nums[1]);
        for (int i = 2; i < nums.length; i++) {
            int curr  = Math.max(prev1, prev2+nums[i]);
            prev2 = prev1;
            prev1 = curr;
        }
        return prev1;
    }

Top-Down Mem Solution :   
        static int minCoins(int[] coins, int amount){
  int[][] dp = new int[coins.length][amount+1];
        for(int i = 0; i < coins.length; i++) Arrays.fill(dp[i], -1);
        int res = coins(coins.length-1, coins, amount, dp);
        if(res == (int) 1e9) return -1;
        return res;
    }

    static int coins(int n, int[] coins, int amount, int[][] dp) {
        if(n == 0) {
            if(amount % coins[0] == 0) return amount/coins[0];
            else return (int) 1e9;
        }
        if(dp[n][amount] != -1) return dp[n][amount];
        int notPick = 0 + coins(n-1, coins, amount, dp);
        int pick = Integer.MAX_VALUE;
        if(coins[n] <= amount) pick = 1 + coins(n, coins, amount - coins[n], dp);
        return dp[n][amount] = Math.min(pick, notPick);
    }

Min no. of coins required to get the given sum - https://www.geeksforgeeks.org/find-minimum-number-of-coins-that-make-a-change/
Solution : 
     int max = amount + 1;
        int[] dp = new int[max];
        Arrays.fill(dp, max);
        dp[0] = 0;

        for (int coin : coins) {
            for (int i = coin; i <= amount; i++) {
                dp[i] = Math.min(dp[i], dp[i - coin] + 1);
            }
        }
        return dp[amount] > amount ? -1 : dp[amount];

    public int cutRod(int price[], int n) {//rod length oriented for loop 
        if( n <= 0) return 0 ;
        int maxProfit = 0 ;
        for(int i = 1 ; i <= n ; i ++){
            int currProfit = price[i-1] + cutRod(price,n-i);
            maxProfit=Math.max(maxProfit,currProfit);
        }
        return maxProfit;
    }
    public int cutRod(int price[],int n){//price[] oriented for loop 
        if(n <= 0) return 0 ; 
        int maxProfit = Integer.MIN_VALUE;
        for(int i = 0 ; i < price.length ;i ++){
            int cut = i + 1 ;
            if(cut  <= n)//i=length-1 cut = length which can produce incorrect profits 
                int currProfit = price[i] + cutRod(price,n-cut);
                maxProfit=Math.max(maxProfit,currProfit);
        }
        return maxProfit ;
    }

    public int cutRod(int price[], int n) {

    public int helper(int[] price,int n, int[] dp){
        if(n <= 0) return 0 ;
        if(dp[n-1] != -1) return dp[n-1];

        for(int i = 1 ; i <= n ; i ++){
            int currProfit = price[i-1] + helper(price,n-i,dp);
            maxProfit=Math.max(maxProfit,currProfit);
                }
                dp[n-1] = maxProfit;
        return maxProfit;
    }

      static int rodCutting(int n, int price[]){
        if(n<=0) return 0 ;//Pretty sure u forgot about this check 
        int[] dp=new int[n+1];
        dp[0]=0;
        dp[1]=price[0];//meaning now below for loop can begin from 2 ?? 
        for(int len = 1;len < n+1 ; len ++){//acc 2 dp dimensions 
                int ans = Integer.MIN_VALUE;
            for(int cut=1; cut<= len ; cut++){//updating ans statement 
                int currProfit = price[cut-1] + dp[len-cut];//Placed dp indices inside price 
                ans = Math.max(ans,currProfit);
            }
            dp[len]=ans;
        }
        return dp[n];
    }

    public int cutRod(int price[], int n) {
    if (n <= 0) {
        return 0; // Base case: if rod length is 0 or negative, return 0 profit
    }

    int maxProfit = 0; // Initialize maxProfit to store the cumulative maximum profit

    for (int i = 1; i <= n; i++) {
        int currProfit = Integer.MIN_VALUE; // Initialize currProfit for current rod length
        for (int j = 1; j <= i; j++) {
            int remainingLength = i - j; // Calculate remaining rod length after cut
            int currPrice = price[j - 1]; // Get price of current cut
            int remainingProfit = maxProfit - currPrice; // Calculate remaining profit from previous cuts
            currProfit = Math.max(currProfit, currPrice + remainingProfit); // Calculate current profit
        }
        maxProfit = currProfit; // Update maxProfit with current profit
    }

    return maxProfit; // Return maxProfit for rod length n
    }

o Find longest increasing subsSequence - https://www.geeksforgeeks.org/longest-increasing-subsequence-dp-3/
Solution : 
     int n = vec.size();
        int[] dp = new int[n];
        int maxLen = 0;

        for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
            dp[i] = 1; // Initialize the length of LIS at index i to 1
            for (int j = 0; j < i; j++) {
                if (vec.get(i) > vec.get(j)) {
                    dp[i] = Math.max(dp[i], dp[j] + 1); // Update the length of LIS at index i
                }
            }
            maxLen = Math.max(maxLen, dp[i]); // Update the maximum length of LIS
        }

        return maxLen;

     bottom-up DP Solution : 
                  int s1Size = s1.length();
        int s2Size = s2.length();
        int[][] dp = new int[s1Size +1 ][s2Size +1];
        for(int i = 0 ; i <s1Size+1 ; i ++){
            for(int j = 0 ; j < s2Size +1 ; j ++){
                if(i == 0){
                    dp[i][j] = j;
                } else if(j == 0){
                    dp[i][j] = i;
                }else if(s1.charAt(i-1) == s2.charAt(j-1)){
                     dp[i][j]=dp[i-1][j-1];//i-1,j-1
                }else{ 
                int insert = dp[i-1][j];
                int delete = dp[i][j-1];
                int update = dp[i-1][j-1];
                dp[i][j]= 1 + Math.min(insert,Math.min(delete,update));
                }
            }
        }
        return dp[s1Size][s2Size];

public static long coinChange(int amount, int n, int []coins) { 
    if(amount <= 0) return 0;

}
private static long helper(int amt,int[] coins,int i){
    if(i >= coins.length || amount < 0) return 0 ;
    if(amount == 0) return 1;
    int dont_pick = helper(amt,coins,i+1);
    int pick = 0 ;
    //doubtful about if same coins is being taken over n over again then what about taking coin[i] n coin[i+1] ? is that not a valid solution approach 
    if(coins[i] <= amt){
          pick =   helper(amt-coins[i],coins,i); //did not return 1 cause of above sol condition   
    }
    return pick + dont_pick;
}
}

public static long coinChange(int amount, int n, int []coins) { 
		return helper(amount,n,0,coins); 
	}  
	public static long helper(int amount,int n ,int i,int[] coins){ 
		if(i == n ) return 0 ; 
		if(amount == 0 ) return 1; 
		long ans = 0 ;// 
		ans = helper(amount,n,i+1,coins); 
		if(amount >= coins[i]){
			ans = ans + helper(amount - coins[i],n,i,coins);
		}
		return ans ;
	}

Solution - 

	public static long coinChange(int amount, int n, int []coins) {
		long[][] dp=new long[n+1][amount+1];
		for(int i = 0 ; i < n+1 ; i ++){
			for(int j = 0 ; j < amount+1 ; j ++){
				dp[i][j]= -1;
			}
		}
		return helper(amount,n,0,coins,dp);
	}
	public static long helper(int amount,int n ,int i,int[] coins,long[][] dp){
		if(i == n) return 0;
		if(amount <= 0) return 1;
		if(dp[i][amount] != -1) return dp[i][amount]; 
		long ans = helper(amount,n,i+1,coins,dp);
		if(coins[i] <= amount){
			 ans = ans + helper(amount - coins[i],n,i,coins,dp);
		}
		dp[i][amount] = ans;
		return ans;
	}

    public boolean canPartition(int[] nums) {
        if(nums.length == 0) return false;
        int totalSum = 0 ; 
        for(int i = 0 ; i < nums.length ; i ++){
            totalSum += nums[i];
        }
        if(totalSum %2 != 0)return false;
        int target = totalSum /2;
        if(target == 0) return true;
        return partition(nums,0,target);
    }
    private boolean partition(int[] nums,int idx,int target){//currTarget may b  
        if(idx == nums.length || target < 0) return false;
        if(target == 0)return true;
        boolean include = partition(nums,idx+1,target-nums[idx]);
        boolean exclude = partition(nums,idx+1,target);
        return include || exclude ;
        //if return 1 and 0 then 
        //Math.max(include,exclude); OR 
        // if(include == 0 && exclude == 0) return 0 else return 1
    }
T.C. : 2^n include and exclude 
S.C. Height of recursion tree which will contain all elements of [] b/t  root and leaf  in the worst case so Linear O(n)

Solution : 

    public boolean canPartition(int[] nums) {
        if(nums.length == 0) return false;
        if(nums.length == 1) return false;
        int totalSum = 0 ; 
        for(int i = 0 ;i < nums.length ; i ++){
            totalSum += nums[i];
        }
        if(totalSum %2 != 0 ) return false;
        int targetSum = totalSum /2 ; 
        int[][] memo=new int[nums.length+1][targetSum+1];
        for(int i = 0 ; i <= nums.length ;i ++)
            Arrays.fill(memo[i],-1);
        return partition(0,targetSum,nums,memo);
    }
    private boolean partition(int idx,int sum , int[] arr,int[][] memo){
        if(sum < 0 || idx >= arr.length) return false;
        if(memo[idx][sum] != -1){
            return memo[idx][sum] == 1 ? true : false;
        }
        if(sum == 0) return true;
        boolean pick = partition(idx+1,sum-arr[idx],arr,memo);
        boolean dont_pick = partition(idx+1,sum,arr,memo);
        boolean ans = pick || dont_pick ;
        memo[idx][sum] = ans == true ? 1 : 0 ;
        return ans; 
    }

        if(nums.length == 0 || nums.lenght == 1)return false;

        if(target == 0) return true;
        int[][] dp=new int[nums.length+1][target+1];
        for(int i=0; i <= nums.length ; i ++){
            dp[i][0] = 1;//For any sum taken from nums if an emptySubset is produced then its true
        }
        //dp[0][0]=1;
        int[] prev=new int[target + 1];
        //A subset of sum 0 is not possible 
        prev[0]=0;
        for(int i=1 ; i <= nums.length ; i ++)
            for(int j = 1 ; j <= target ; j ++)
              if(nums[i-1] > j){ 
              dp[i][j] = dp[i-1][j];
              }else{
                int include = dp[i-1][j - nums[i-1]];
                int exclude = dp[i-1][j];
                dp[i][j] = Math.max(include,exclude);
              }
        return dp[nums.length][target] > 0 ? true : false; 
        ____________OR below solution ___________________
       public boolean canPartition(int[] nums) {
        if(nums.length == 0)return false;
        int targetSum = 0 ; 
        for(int i = 0 ; i < nums.length ; i ++){
            targetSum += nums[i];
        }       
        //sum  is odd then not possible to partition the array into two equal sum 
        if(targetSum %2 != 0)return false;
        int target = targetSum/2;
        if(target == 0) return true;
        // Create a int array dp to store whether it's possible to achieve a sum j using elements up to index i
        int[][] dp=new int[nums.length+1][target+1];
            // Base case: It's always possible to achieve a sum of 0 with an empty subset
            //0 length array divide it into 2 -> 0 each of the two so equally distributed 
            //By the way I think that whenever the target decreases to 0 we were returning true or 1 as seen in recursion  
        dp[0][0]=1;
        for(int i=1 ; i <= nums.length ; i ++)
            for(int j = 1 ; j <= target ; j ++)
              if(nums[i-1] > j){ 
              dp[i][j] = dp[i-1][j];
              }else{
                int include = dp[i-1][j - nums[i-1]];
                int exclude = dp[i-1][j];
                dp[i][j] = Math.max(include,exclude);
              }
        return dp[nums.length][target] > 0 ? true : false; 
        //OR return dp[nums.length][target] == 1 
    }

Merge Intervals 
An interval is a range, with a starting value and ending value. [1, 3] indicates elements 1, 2, 3 and so on.

Given a collection of intervals, merge all overlapping intervals. The result should only have mutually exclusive intervals - meaning that no number should be common between two intervals, in the result.

Note: The merged intervals should be printed in increasing order of start value.

Input format
There are N+1 lines of input.

First line contains N, the number of intervals

Next N lines contain 2 space separated integers A and B, which represent the start and end of an interval

Output format
For the X merged intervals, print each interval (the start and end being space separated) on a separate line

Constraints
1 <= N <= 50000

0 <= A, B <= 1e9

B >= A

Sample Input 1
4

1 3

2 6

8 10

15 18

Sample Output 1
1 6

8 10

15 18

Explanation 1
Since intervals [1 3] and [2 6] overlap, merge them into [1 6]

Sample Input 2
2

1 4

4 5

Sample Output 2
1 5

Explanation 2
Intervals [1 4] and [4 5] overlap and get merged into [1 5]
    givenFunc(int[][] intervals){
    Arrays.sort(intervals, (a, b) -> Integer.compare(a[0], b[0]));
        
        List<int[]> merged = new ArrayList<>();
        
        for (int[] interval : intervals) {
        
            if (merged.isEmpty() || merged.get(merged.size() - 1)[1] < interval[0]) {
                merged.add(interval);
            } else {
                int[] lastInterval = merged.get(merged.size() - 1);
                lastInterval[1] = Math.max(lastInterval[1], interval[1]);
            }
        }
        
        return merged.toArray(new int[merged.size()][]);
    }
Given two strings s and t, write a function to determine if t is an anagram of s.

Note: You may assume the string contains only lowercase alphabets.

Note:-
There's a test case where both the strings are empty but the js compiler is treating one as empty and other as undefined. So, update the readline function accordingly.

Input format
You will be given two strings in two separate lines.

Output format
Print "true" if both the strings are anagram otherwise “false”.

Constraints
Length of string <= 100000

Sample Input 1
anagram

nagaram

Sample Output 1
true

Sample Input 2
rat

car

Sample Output 2
false

Solution 
      if (s == null || t == null) return false;
        if (s.length() != t.length()) return false;

        int[] count = new int[26];
        for (int i = 0; i < s.length(); i++) {
            count[s.charAt(i) - 'a']++;
            count[t.charAt(i) - 'a']--;
        }

        for (int c : count) {
            if (c != 0) return false;
        }
        return true;

A proper prefix sum array is a prefix sum array without the entire array sum, that is, with the last element of a normal prefix sum array missing. Thus, for a = [1, 2, 3, 4], the proper prefix sum array, pps = [1, 3, 6].

Similarly, a proper suffix sum array is a suffix sum array without the entire array sum, that is, with the first element of a normal suffix sum array missing. For the above example, the proper suffix sum array, pss = [9, 7, 4].

A magic sum is a non negative sum that’ll exist in both the pps and the pss.

Given an array of size n, you have to find the largest magic sum, that is, the largest non negative element that exists in both the pps and the pss. If no such element exists, return -1.

Note:- A proper prefix and proper suffix of an array is not equal to the array itself and non - empty.

Input format
First line contains an integer n, the size of the array. Second line contains n space separated integers, representing the elements of the array.

Output format
Print the max magic sum in the array if it exists, else print -1.

Sample Input 1
5

1 2 3 4 10

Sample Output 1
10

Explanation
Proper Prefix Sums are - [1, 3, 6, 10]

Proper Suffix Sums are - [19, 17, 14, 10]

10 is the only common element, thus, 10 is the answer.

Constraints
1 <= n <= 10^5

-10^6 <= array elements <= 10^6

  public int uniquePaths(int m, int n) {
               int[][] dp = new int[m][n];
        
        // Initialize the first row to 1 (only one way to reach cells in the first row)
        for (int i = 0; i < m; i++) {
            dp[i][0] = 1;
        }
        
        // Initialize the first column to 1 (only one way to reach cells in the first column)
        for (int j = 0; j < n; j++) {
            dp[0][j] = 1;
        }
        
        // Calculate the number of unique paths to each cell based on the number of paths to its top and left neighbors
        for (int i = 1; i < m; i++) {
            for (int j = 1; j < n; j++) {
                dp[i][j] = dp[i - 1][j] + dp[i][j - 1];
            }
        }
        
        // Return the number of unique paths to the bottom-right corner
        return dp[m - 1][n - 1];
    }

        boolean[][] dp = new boolean[n][n];
        // All substrings of length 1 are palindromic
        for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
            dp[i][i] = true;
        }
        
        // Check for substrings of length 2
        for (int i = 0; i < n - 1; i++) {
            if (str.charAt(i) == str.charAt(i + 1)) {
                dp[i][i + 1] = true;
                maxLength = 2;
            }
        }
        
        // Check for substrings of length greater than 2
        for (int len = 3; len <= n; len++) {
            for (int start = 0; start < n - len + 1; start++) {
                int end = start + len - 1;
                if (str.charAt(start) == str.charAt(end) && dp[start + 1][end - 1]) {
                    dp[start][end] = true;
                    maxLength = Math.max(maxLength, len);
                }
            }
        }
        
        return maxLength;      int maxLength = 1; 

Rotate Image matrix question 
private void rotateImage(int[][] matrix){
      int n = matrix.length;
        
        // Step 1: Transpose the matrix (swap matrix[i][j] with matrix[j][i])
        for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
            for (int j = i + 1; j < n; j++) {
                // Swap matrix[i][j] and matrix[j][i]
                int temp = matrix[i][j];
                matrix[i][j] = matrix[j][i];
                matrix[j][i] = temp;
            }
        }
        
        // Step 2: Reverse each row
        for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
            int left = 0;
            int right = n - 1;
            
            while (left < right) {
                // Swap elements at left and right positions
                int temp = matrix[i][left];
                matrix[i][left] = matrix[i][right];
                matrix[i][right] = temp;
                
                left++;
                right--;
            }
        }
    }
    
    // Helper method to print matrix
    public void printMatrix(int[][] matrix) {
        for (int i = 0; i < matrix.length; i++) {
            for (int j = 0; j < matrix[i].length; j++) {
                System.out.print(matrix[i][j]);
                if (j < matrix[i].length - 1) {
                    System.out.print(" ");
                }
            }
            System.out.println();
        }
    }

Two-pointer technique:

Involves using two pointers (usually initialized at different positions) to solve problems that require iteration or comparison over elements in an array or list.
Common applications include finding pairs with a specific sum, reversing an array, or checking for palindromes.

Sliding window technique:

Involves using a window (represented by two pointers or indices) to track a subset of elements within an array or string.
The window slides or expands as you iterate through the data structure, and it's particularly useful for solving problems that involve finding subarrays or
substrings with specific properties, such as maximum sum subarray, minimum window substring, or longest substring without repeating characters.

We can consider graphs as a data structure where data stored in the form of nodes/vertices contained within directed or un-directed edges. When a directed graph is being considered then 
there exists edges from a given node/vetex to a given node/verted . Whereas in case of undirected graphs we can freely traverse back and forth between two vertices freely(BFS) 
This is also referred to as degree of a graph's NODE . For undirected graph it would include all the edges associated with that node , whereas in case of directed graph we have   
inDegree and outDegree. U know what it means  . Also graphs can have weights assigned to thier edges too , such graphs are called WeightedGraphs Path may be defined as that  
sequence of steps followed to traverse along the vertices such that each vertex is visited exactly once . Cause if this condition is violated then it would be a CYCLIC graph which is  
usually directed . Directed edges may turn a graph into a cyclic one  

Types of Graphs : 
o Cyclic & Non-Cyclic 
o Connected & Disconnected
o Directed & Un-Directed 
o Weighted & un-weighted 
Adjacency Matrix refers to the representation of edge conncections which exists in the given graph .  Where indices indicate vertices and edges . If 4 da given data e and v match 
            there will be true .
Adjacency List : usually map which represents the connections a given node has with its neighbours depending upon the un/directed edges it contains  . where key = int val=list<>
        cause in case of vector we would need int as key at all times whereas in case of  list we can have whatever as the key

detect a cylcle in a directed graph - https://www.geeksforgeeks.org/detect-cycle-in-a-graph/ 
Solution :  
             static boolean isCyclic(int node, List<List<Integer>> graph, boolean[] visited, boolean[] recStack) {
        if (recStack[node]) {
                return true; // Back edge found, cycle detected
            }
            if (visited[node]) {
                return false; // Node already visited, no cycle
            }

            visited[node] = true;
            recStack[node] = true;

            for (int neighbor : graph.get(node)) {
                if (isCyclic(neighbor, graph, visited, recStack)) {
                    return true; // Cycle found in neighbor's subtree
                }
            }

            recStack[node] = false;
            return false;
            }

        static int cycleDirectedGraph(int n, int[][] edges){

                List<List<Integer>> graph = new ArrayList<>();
            for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
                graph.add(new ArrayList<>());
            }

            for (int[] edge : edges) {
                graph.get(edge[0] - 1).add(edge[1] - 1); // Adjusting 1-based indexing to 0-based indexing
            }

            boolean[] visited = new boolean[n];
            boolean[] recStack = new boolean[n];

            for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
                if (isCyclic(i, graph, visited, recStack)) {
                    return 1; // Cycle found
                }
            }

            return 0; // No cycle found
            }

          private static void addEdge(ArrayList<Integer>[] adj, int u, int v) {
            adj[u].add(v);
        }
     private static void dfs(ArrayList<Integer>[] adj, int[] col, int curr, boolean[] isCyclic) {
            col[curr] = 1;

            for (int x : adj[curr]) {
                if (col[x] == 1) {
                    isCyclic[0] = true;
                    return;
                } else if (col[x] == 0) {
                    dfs(adj, col, x, isCyclic);
                }
            }

            col[curr] = 2;
        }
      private static boolean checkCycle(ArrayList<Integer>[] adj, int[] col, int k) {
            boolean[] isCyclic = { false };
            for (int i = 0; i < k; i++) {
                if (col[i] == 0) {
                    dfs(adj, col, i, isCyclic);
                }
            }
            return isCyclic[0];
        }     
          private static void topologicalSortUtil(ArrayList<Integer>[] adj, int u, boolean[] visited, Stack<Integer> st) {
            visited[u] = true;
            for (int v : adj[u]) {
                if (!visited[v]) {
                    topologicalSortUtil(adj, v, visited, st);
                }
            }
            st.push(u);
        }
     private static String topologicalSort(ArrayList<Integer>[] adj, int V) {
            boolean[] visited = new boolean[V];
            Stack<Integer> st = new Stack<>();

            for (int i = 0; i < V; i++) {
                if (!visited[i]) {
                    topologicalSortUtil(adj, i, visited, st);
                }
            }

            StringBuilder order = new StringBuilder();
            while (!st.isEmpty()) {
                order.append((char) (st.pop() + 'a'));
            }
            return order.toString();
        }
     private static String alienDictionary(String words[]) {
            int n = words.length;
            int[] frq = new int[26];

            // Count of unique characters
            int k = 0;

            // Count unique characters and their frequencies
            for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
                String s = words[i];
                for (int j = 0; j < s.length(); j++) {
                    frq[s.charAt(j) - 'a']++;
                    if (frq[s.charAt(j) - 'a'] == 1)
                        k++;
                }
            }

            // Create adjacency list for the graph
            ArrayList<Integer>[] adj = new ArrayList[k];
            for (int i = 0; i < k; i++) {
                adj[i] = new ArrayList<>();
            }

            // Build the graph by iterating through adjacent words
            for (int i = 0; i < n - 1; i++) {
                String word1 = words[i];
                String word2 = words[i + 1];

                int j = 0;
                while (j < word1.length() && j < word2.length()) {
                    if (word1.charAt(j) != word2.charAt(j)) {
                        // Add edges based on character order
                        addEdge(adj, word1.charAt(j) - 'a', word2.charAt(j) - 'a');
                        break;
                    }
                    j++;
                }
            }

            // Color array for cycle detection
            int[] col = new int[k];
            if (checkCycle(adj, col, k)) {
                // Detect and handle cycles
                return "-1";
            }

            // Perform topological sorting and return character order
            return topologicalSort(adj, k);
        }
    Solution passing all : 

          private static String alienDictionary(Vector<String> vec) {

            Map<Character, Set<Character>> graph = new HashMap<>();
            Map<Character, Integer> inDegree = new HashMap<>();

            // Initialize the inDegree map
            for (String word : vec) {
                for (char c : word.toCharArray()) {
                    inDegree.put(c, 0);
                }
            }

            // Build the graph and calculate in-degrees
            for (int i = 0; i < vec.size() - 1; i++) {
                String word1 = vec.get(i);
                String word2 = vec.get(i + 1);
                int minLength = Math.min(word1.length(), word2.length());
                for (int j = 0; j < minLength; j++) {
                    char parent = word1.charAt(j);
                    char child = word2.charAt(j);
                    if (parent != child) {
                        graph.computeIfAbsent(parent, k -> new HashSet<>());
                        if (!graph.get(parent).contains(child)) {
                            graph.get(parent).add(child);
                            inDegree.put(child, inDegree.get(child) + 1);
                        }
                        break;
                    }
                    // For cases like "abc" and "ab", where "abc" should come after "ab"
                    if (j == minLength - 1 && word1.length() > word2.length()) {
                        return "-1";
                    }
                }
            }

            // Perform topological sort
            StringBuilder result = new StringBuilder();
            Queue<Character> queue = new LinkedList<>();
            for (char c : inDegree.keySet()) {
                if (inDegree.get(c) == 0) {
                    queue.add(c);
                }
            }
            while (!queue.isEmpty()) {
                char current = queue.poll();
                result.append(current);
                if (graph.containsKey(current)) {
                    for (char neighbor : graph.get(current)) {
                        inDegree.put(neighbor, inDegree.get(neighbor) - 1);
                        if (inDegree.get(neighbor) == 0) {
                            queue.add(neighbor);
                        }
                    }
                }
            }

            if (result.length() < inDegree.size()) {
                return "-1"; // There is a cycle in the graph
            }

            return result.toString();
            }}

Fast And Slow Pointers 
hare = 2 x tortoise 

TOPOLOGICAL SORT :  
ordering of vertices of graph such that if there is an edge existing between u and v then u would occur before v .In order to atttempt task v we need 
to complete task u(u->v)
There can be  multiple topo sorts for the exact same DAGraph (acyclic graph).  
It is a Linear time complexitz algorithem i.e. O(no.ofVertices + no.ofEdges )[algthough the number of edges are usually more so O(nE)] 
 Over here we will be using a stack for the LIFO ordering which will gradually produce the Topo sort.We would add elements into the stack 
only when the DFS calls for all the adjacent elements of the current node has been made . Acyclic cause otherwise if a cycle exists then it would cause
 a deadlock of courses because 
in order to take one course1 one will have to take course2 which in turn will denpend on course3 which is also a depending factor of course 1 

Depth First Search : use stack  
Keep visiting nodes as long as there's a valid path . Else push the last visited node in the stk then back track !  
Or if you back-tracked and came across a visited array , push it to the stack then backtrack  
 
Kahn'sAlgo : BFS so use Q  
is the BFS approach towards solving this problem :  
o Calculate the inDegree of all nodes

o Came across new nodes with 0 inDegree ? push inside Q else ignore them just continue  
o 1 pop out Q's front/head  
o 2 put inside answer D.S. letZ say ArrayList<>  
o 3 visit its neighbours  
o 4 decrease neighbors of above neighbors by 1  
Question - Find Topological Order : 
    Has More links in this link https://www.crio.do/learn/PSDS/ME_PS_DS_CONCEPT_GRAPH/ME_PS_DS_CONCEPT_GRAPH_MODULE_TOPOLOGICALORDERING/assessment/
    CRIO GRAPH https://www.crio.do/learn/PSDS/ME_PS_DS_CONCEPT_GRAPH/
    Topological Sort of a directed graph is a linear ordering of its vertices such that for every directed edge (U,V) from vertex U to vertex V, U comes before V in the ordering.

    Given a directed graph, find the Topological ordering of its vertices.

    Note: A valid topological ordering of the graph will always be present i.e., there will be no cycle.

    Input format
    First line contains two space separated integers N and E, when N represents the number of vertices and E represents the number of directed edges, respectively.

    Next E lines contain two space separated integers U and V, specifying a directed edge from vertex U to vertex V. (Vertices are numbered from 1 to N)

    Output format
    Print the space separate vertex numbers in Topological order

    Constraints
    N <= 500

    1 <= E <= min(N*(N-1)/2,100000)

    1 <= U,V <= N

    Sample Input 1
    5 3

    1 2

    1 3

    4 5

    Sample Output 1
    1 4 2 3 5

    Explanation 1
    There are multiple solutions possible for this example. In each solution 1 should come before 2 & 3, and 4 should come before 5.

    One such other solution is {1 2 4 3 5}

Solution HashMap intial test cases passed BUT TLE :  
    public boolean canFinish(int numCourses, int[][] prerequisites) {
    Map<Integer, List<Integer>> adjMap = new HashMap<>();
        for (int[] preReq : prerequisites) {
            int course = preReq[0];
            int prerequisite = preReq[1];
            List<Integer> dependentCourses = adjMap.getOrDefault(prerequisite, new ArrayList<>());
            //dependentCourses so why not prerequisite
            dependentCourses.add(course);
            adjMap.put(prerequisite, dependentCourses);
        }

        // Visited array to track visited courses
        boolean[] visited = new boolean[numCourses];
        // Stack to perform a topological sort
        Stack<Integer> stack = new Stack<>();

        // Perform a topological sort for each unvisited course
        for (int course = 0; course < numCourses; course++) {
            if (!visited[course] && dfs(adjMap, visited, stack, course)) {
                return false;
            }
        }

        return true;
    }

    // Depth-First Search to detect cycles
    private boolean dfs(Map<Integer, List<Integer>> adjMap, boolean[] visited, Stack<Integer> stack, int course) {
        visited[course] = true;
        stack.push(course);

        if (adjMap.containsKey(course)) {
            for (int nextCourse : adjMap.get(course)) {
                if (!visited[nextCourse]) {
                    if (dfs(adjMap, visited, stack, nextCourse)) {
                        return true;
                    }
                } else if (visited[nextCourse] && stack.contains(nextCourse)) {
                    // Cycle detected
                    return true;
                }
            }
        }

        // Backtrack after processing all dependent courses
        stack.pop();
        visited[course] = false;
        return false;
    }

Solution DFS:
    	   private static void dfs(int node, boolean[] visited, Map<Integer, List<Integer>> graph, Stack<Integer> stack) {
                visited[node] = true;
                for (int neighbor : graph.getOrDefault(node, new ArrayList<>())) {
                    if (!visited[neighbor]) {
                        dfs(neighbor, visited, graph, stack);
                    }
                }
                stack.push(node);
            }

    private static Vector<Integer> topologicalOrdering(int n, Vector<Vector<Integer>> edges) {
        Map<Integer, List<Integer>> graph = new HashMap<>();
        //Method I 
        for(int i = 0 ; i < edges.size() ; i ++){
            Vector<Integer> edge = edges.get(i);
            //u -> v so v should be 0 while u should 1 
            int u = edge.get(0);
            int v = edge.get(1);
            if(!graph.containsKey(u)){
                graph.put(u,new ArrayList<>());
            }
            graph.get(u).add(v);
        }
        //Method II 
        // for (Vector<Integer> edge : edges) { 
        //     int u = edge.get(0);
        //     int v = edge.get(1); 
        //     graph.computeIfAbsent(u, key -> new ArrayList<>()).add(v); 
        // } 
        boolean[] visited = new boolean[n + 1];//TODO:?
        Stack<Integer> stack = new Stack<>();

        for (int i = 1; i <= n; i++) {
            if (!visited[i]) {
                dfs(i, visited, graph, stack);
            }
        }

        Vector<Integer> topologicalOrder = new Vector<>();
        while (!stack.isEmpty()) {
            topologicalOrder.add(stack.pop());
        }
        return topologicalOrder;
    }

Kahn's Algo  
1 create an adjList  
2 create an inDegree[]  
3 with the node of 0 inDegree(ask interviewer if always will there be a course with 0 inDegree) push inside a Q (since bfs)  
4 pop out the Q's head and put it inside ans[]  
5 look for its neighbors in the adjList and decrease their inDegree by 1 or -- ;  
6 repeat until coming across a visited node || no node left to visit or null

Solution 
    public int[] findOrder(int numCourses, int[][] preq) {
        int[] inDegree = new int[numCourses];
        Map<Integer,List<Integer>> adjList = new HashMap<>();
        for(int i = 0 ; i < preq.length ;i ++){
                int course = preq[i][0];
                int prevCourse = preq[i][1];
                if(!adjList.containsKey(prevCourse)) adjList.put(prevCourse,new ArrayList<Integer>());
                adjList.get(prevCourse).add(course);
                inDegree[course] += 1;                
        }
        Queue<Integer> zeroDegree=new LinkedList<>();
        for(int i = 0 ; i < inDegree.length ;i ++){
            if(inDegree[i] == 0) zeroDegree.offer(i); 
        }
        int[] orderArray = new int[numCourses]; //TODO: Topological ordering ? 
        int orderIdx = 0 ;
        while(!zeroDegree.isEmpty()){
            int currCourse = zeroDegree.poll();
            orderArray[orderIdx++]= currCourse;
            if(adjList.containsKey(currCourse)){
                //any situation that it would not contain the currCourse or was it handled previously itself at the point of creating the adjacencyList ? 
                List<Integer> preqCourseList = adjList.get(currCourse);
                if(preqCourseList.size() == 0) break;
                for(int i = 0 ; i < preqCourseList.size() ; i ++){
                    int currPrevCourse = preqCourseList.get(i);
                    inDegree[currPrevCourse] -= 1;
                    if(inDegree[currPrevCourse] == 0){//was doubtful if we should have this if statement inside the for loop or not or have 2 for s inside while
                        zeroDegree.offer(currPrevCourse);
                    }
                }
            }
        }
        return orderIdx != numCourses ? new int[0] : orderArray;
    }

        colors[node]=color ;

    String bipartiteCheck(int[][] graph){
        int nums = graph.length;
        Map<Integer,ArryList<Integer>> adjList=new HashMap<>();
        int[] colors = new int[nums];
        for(int i = 0 ; i < nums; i ++){
                int u = graph[i][0];
                int v = graph[i][1];//u<-v means v is the pre-qrequisite for u or v comes before u HOWEVER undirected so we will add entries  
                adjList.computeIfAbsent(u,new ArrayList<Integer>()).add(v);
                adjList.computeIfAbsent(v,new ArrayList<Integer>()).add(u);
                OR if(!adjList.containsKey(u)){adjList.put(u,new ArrayList<>());} adjList.get(u).add(v);
                 if(!adjList.containsKey(V)){adjList.put(v,new ArrayList<>());} adjList.get(v).add(u);
        }
        for(int i = 0 ; i < nums ; i ++){
            if(colors[i] == 0 && !dfs(colors,graph,i,1)){
                return "Not Bipartite !" 
            }
        }
        return "Bipartite !"
    }

only after being checked that they have not been visited once , we'll add this elem FIRST into the Q then all the adjacent nodes to the Queue followed by updating their visited status 
later we will move FIFO the element out of the queue also inserting it up in our resulting vector, LEVEL ORDER TRAVERSAL

Shortest Path in Undirected Graph : After creating adj u can look for the parents of all the nodes via the  unordered visited map . BFS would be used where condition for pushing  
 into the Q would be the elements which are the children of the corresponding parent being traversed from the vis[] . U can store the parents of the various elements in an array  
 which can later for traversing from target to the source order later this order can be reversed  
 NOTES

Greedy Algo which looks for best benefit from the info available @ that point of time (we don't move back to past decisions for changes as seen in backtracking) 
Algo for finding the minimum distance between a given source node to all the nodes/target . A Greedy Algo which aims at choosing the best available option on the basis of the  
Available info . Decision with the most immediate benefit and move on without any need to backTrack .Great for searching the path with the lowest cost in a weighted directed graph  
or may be sum of costs , product of weights or max weights Only condition it has is the cost are required to be NON-DECREASING at all times(for such cases Belmont&FordAlgo)

minHeap.offerOrDefault(0,source); 
while minHeapQ is not empty :  
    leastDistanceNode,currNode = minHeap.pop() ;/pair so two values   
    if(visited[leastDistanceNode]) continue ; //why 2 revisit ?Else we mark is visited below   
    visited[leastDistanceNode]; 
    for i=0;i<graph.size;i++// check for currNode's neighbours (cost of course)  
        int neighbourDistance = dist[currNeighbour] + weight of edge from currNode->currNeighbour    
        if(!visited[currNeighbor] && neighbourDistance < dist[currNeighbor]) //if true than we found a better path so update it in dist[],prev[] and minHeap   
                dist[currNeighbour] = neighbourDistance;  
                prev[currNeighbor] = currNode;  
                minHeap.push(Pair<neighbourDistance,currNeighbor>);   
    return dist,prev;

Solution : 
 Map<Integer, List<int[]>> graph = new HashMap<>();
        for (int i = 0; i < times.length; i++) {
            int u = times[i][0];
            int v = times[i][1];
            int w = times[i][2];
            if (!graph.containsKey(u)) {
                graph.put(u, new ArrayList<>());
            }
            graph.get(u).add(new int[]{v, w});
        }
        
        int[] dist = new int[N + 1];
        Arrays.fill(dist, Integer.MAX_VALUE);
        dist[K] = 0;
        PriorityQueue<int[]> pq = new PriorityQueue<>(Comparator.comparingInt(a -> a[1]));
        pq.add(new int[]{K, 0});
        
        while (!pq.isEmpty()) {
            int[] current = pq.poll();
            int u = current[0];
            int time = current[1];
            
            if (time > dist[u]) continue;
            
            if (graph.containsKey(u)) {
                List<int[]> neighbors = graph.get(u);
                for (int i = 0; i < neighbors.size(); i++) {
                    int[] neighbor = neighbors.get(i);
                    int v = neighbor[0];
                    int w = neighbor[1];
                    int newDist = dist[u] + w;
                    if (newDist < dist[v]) {
                        dist[v] = newDist;
                        pq.add(new int[]{v, newDist});
                    }
                }
            }
        }
        
        int maxDist = 0;
        for (int i = 1; i <= N; i++) {
            if (dist[i] == Integer.MAX_VALUE) return -1;
            maxDist = Math.max(maxDist, dist[i]);
        }
        
        return maxDist;

Those who don't know their pa st are condemned to repeat it !  One can obtain the optimal solution of a given problem by considering the 
(I)OPT.SOL of its 
(II) overlapping subproblems  
1->TopDown : Recursion + memoization(Storage for the overlapping subproblems values of a given big problem) usually a map or table(can b an[]) used Here we begin fro m the 
given problem's large value itself and gruadually store the data in a DS(vector dp(si+1,-1)) else dp[x]=x*recursiveFunction(x-1); But because we don't know the ans  for the previous 
recursive call we will first be required to move down the recursion tree in order to know the value to the sub-problems. ' . Stack f-call consumption would be high 
2->BottomUp(STATE) : Tabulation Start from the most simple sub-problem and follow a gradual approach towards solving the given problem That is to say starting value of  
ar[0]=1 forFact! . No recursion needed . ' . no load on the function_call stack  
Faster approach than Memization because we know the anwer to the first function-call/simplest sub-problem(We can directly access the First?Prev element) Whereas above we  
look for the answers for previous sub-problem which in turn looks for its previous until down the leaf of the recursion tree is reached. ' . Function-Cal stack memory Consumption inc 
Tabulation requires all the sub-problems to be solved at least once before solving the given bigger problem . Whereas in Memoization only the sub-problems are altered from -1 to  
val INCLUDEs AN ELSE STATEMENT 
 Here we will start from the base case as  the initial value for the same DP DS while keeping the BASE CASE intact  +  this will  change the  LOOP i's starting value and move to the  
3->Space optimization            We won't even be required to have a visited array in this case . ' . SPACE GETS REDUCED since no visited array  
. ' . T.C may still remain linear however space gets reduced .

SubArray : these are also required to be contiguous in nature thereby the order of the array will be preserved at all times 
Subsequence : non-contiguous subset produced from removing or deleting elements from two subsets of the parent string . Doesn't include empty elements

(I) Copy the base case

(III) Copy the recurrence relation

    int helper(int i,int j, string& t1,string &t2,vector<vector<int>> dp)
    {
        if(i-1<0 || j-1<0)return 0; // i==0 || j==0
        if(dp[i][j]!=-1)return dp[i][j];
        if(t1[i-1]==t2[j-1]) return dp[i][j]=1+helper(i-1,j-1,t1,t2,dp);
        return dp[i][j]=max(helper(i,j-1,t1,t2,dp),helper(i-1,j,t1,t2,dp));
    }
    int longestCommonSubsequence(string text1, string text2) {
        int si1=text1.size();
        int si2=text2.size();
        vector<vector<int>> dp(si1+1,vector<int>(si2+1,-1)); 
        return  helper(si1,si2,text1,text2,dp);
    }//OR BELOW   
    
    return dp[si1][si2];
